Implementation consequences:

- **Treat `d42` as the current Plan 6 bridge.** The pair-compatible corner ladder is already present; Plan 6 adds provenance and possible future polish detail.
- **Keep `d44` and the off-pass/back-set triangle family behind D101.** Plan 6 confirms these are 4-player source forms, not hidden pair drills.
- **Do not classify the wash drill as a setting fundamental.** It is a modified game that happens to live inside a setting practice; future catalog work should route it through game-play / attack support.
- **Preserve source title ambiguity.** `Triangle Setting (Serve/Toss)` should not be treated as purely live-serve or purely toss-fed until future authoring decides whether to split variants.

### Practice Plan 7 — full text (verbatim founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **first BAB attacking practice plan captured at source-detail level**, and it introduces the high-line / cut-shot accuracy box geometry, the +3/-3 shot-target scoring wrapper for attack accuracy, the open-net swing pattern, the 2-ball alternating side-out format, and competitive transition with a short-attack constraint line.

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** (15 min): Same universal BAB opener source family captured in Plans 1–6.

- Pass back and forth — 10 each
- Set back and forth — 10 each
- Tomahawk back and forth — 10 each
- Pokey back and forth — 10 each
- Open hand one-handed slap pepper
- Speed pepper — push the speed on the dig, set, and attack
- Defender only: starting from knees to lay-down sprawl dig — 8 each side
- Blocker only: pull digs — 8 each side
- 5 game serves to a passer — pass and catch — each player
- Cross-court dig to a cut shot — setter catches cut shot — 5 each player per side
- Water

**Drill 2 — Triangle Setting** (10 min): Same three-player pass-set-reset triangle source family captured in Plans 5 and 6. All players are on the south side. Player 1 is at the net straight in front of Player 2 in serve-receive position. Player 3 starts in the other passing position next to Player 2. Player 1 tosses or hits to Player 2; Player 2 passes to middle court about 5 ft from net; Player 3 sets back to Player 1, who catches and tosses the next ball or hits back to Player 2. After 10 reps switch positions; once everyone has set, switch sides of the court.

**Drill 3 — Cross Court Pepper** (10 min): Same four-player cross-court pepper source family captured in Plan 5. Players 1 and 2 are on the north side; Players 3 and 4 are on the south side. Imagine Player 1 in northwest, Player 2 in northeast, Player 3 in southeast, and Player 4 in southwest. Round 1: Players 2 and 4 dig and attack while Players 1 and 3 are "blocking" and setting. Each side gets three touches: pass, set, and controlled attack. The drill starts with a toss to Player 2, who passes for Player 1 to set; Player 2 attacks the set with a controlled hit to Player 4. Player 4 digs for Player 3 to set, then Player 4 hits it back to Player 2. Continue for a rep count or back-and-forth goal, then switch roles. Allow both players to dig and hit from each side.

**Drill 4 — +3/-3 Highlines - Cut Shots / HL** (30 min): Player 1 is on the south side; Players 2 and 3 are on the north side. Draw a 4×4 box in either the high-line or the cut-shot location as a target for the player on offense.

- Player 1 bowls or serves the ball to Player 2
- Player 2 passes to Player 3
- Player 3 sets Player 2
- Player 2 shoots for the high-line or cut-shot box. If it lands in the box, Player 2 gets +1; if Player 2 misses, it is -1. Play until Player 2 reaches +3 or -3.

**Drill 5 — Highlines - Cuts - Open Net Swing** (20 min): Players 1 and 2 are on the north side; Players 3 and 4 are on the south side. Player 1 tosses, Player 2 blocks. Players 3 and 4 are passing, setting, and then doing a designated shot. Start with a high-line shot first. Player 1 tosses the ball to either Player 3 or Player 4, who passes for the other player to set so the passer can attack a high-line shot. Player 1 digs the high-line for Player 2 to set, then Player 1 attacks on an **open net** (no blocker). Repeat so all players can be the defender. Once everyone has been the defender, switch to a cut shot instead of a high line and repeat. The defender should always sit in the cross court.

**Drill 6 — 2 Ball Side Out** (20 min): Before starting, draw two lines parallel to the sidelines about 3 ft from each sideline. Inside that new box, draw two more lines: one about 4–5 ft from the net and one about 4–5 ft from the endline. This creates a high-line box and a cut-shot box for both players. Player 1 is on the north side acting as the coach, with all the boxes. Players 2 and 3 are on the south side working on attack accuracy.

- Player 1 tosses the ball to Player 2
- Player 2 passes to Player 3
- Player 3 sets Player 2
- Player 2 hits a high line landing in the box
- Immediately after the ball lands, Player 1 tosses a scrambled free ball to Player 3
- Player 3 passes to Player 2
- Player 2 sets Player 3
- Player 3 hits a cut shot
- Repeat steps 1–8 alternating who receives the first toss
- Repeat so each attacker hits 5 high lines and 5 cut shots, then switch positions

**Drill 7 — Comp Transition HL - CS - Live** (20 min): Before starting, draw a line from sideline to sideline on the south side about 15 ft from the net. Players 1 and 2 are Team A on the north side. Players 3 and 4 are Team B on the south side. Team A starts as the tossing team and Team B is receiving. The first attack from the south side should be a high line, and the first contact from the north side should be a **short attack** in front of the drawn line.

- Team A tosses to Team B
- The Team B player who passes hits a high line
- The defender on Team A runs down and digs the high line from Team B
- The Team A defender attacks the dig so it lands in front of the drawn line on the court
- Finish the play as if it is a live game
- Repeat by tossing to the other Team B player
- Alternate the tosses for 8 rounds, then switch sides of the net with Team A

### Practice Plan 7 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 7 is the first attack-focused BAB plan in the captured set, and it is structurally a **shot-accuracy and game-transition** plan more than a hitting-mechanics plan. The technique-level "how to hit" lives in BAB Beginner's Guide Lesson 3, in Plans 8 and 11 (captured at TOC level only), and in `Pass Set Spike to Perimeter` from Plans 1 and 3. Plan 7 assumes the attacker can already produce a high line and a cut shot, then drills accuracy under increasing constraint: open box → +3/-3 scored box → open-net swing → 2-ball alternating sideout → live competitive transition with a short-attack rule.

This is also the first source evidence in the archive for BAB's **attack-accuracy box convention** (4×4 marked targets in the high-line or cut-shot positions, plus the more elaborate two-shot box geometry in 2 Ball Side Out). That convention is distinct from BAB's serving zones (Plan 2: 4 / 6 / 8 quadrants), distinct from BAB's 7-zone Around-the-World attack ladder (Plans 1, 4), and distinct from FIVB's 5-zone attack convention (Drill 5.6). It is closer to a per-shot scoring rectangle than to a numbered-zone ladder. Future attack-chain authoring should pick its convention deliberately and document the choice.

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Plan 7 is attack-only-by-name.** Every drill except Drill 1 trains attack as the scored skill, but the supporting touches (pass and set) are present in every chain. This reinforces Thesis T1 in `docs/research/practice-plan-authoring-synthesis.md`: a focus is a session purpose, not a single skill tag. A future attack-focused Volleycraft plan should still include passing and setting touches in service of the attack outcome.
- **No M001 catalog bridge exists.** Unlike Plan 5 (`d40 Footwork for Setting`) and Plan 6 (`d42 Corner to Corner Setting`), Plan 7 has zero current app records — `attack` is not a shipped `SkillFocus` and there is no current attack-target drill in `app/src/data/drills.ts`. All Plan 7 drills are Tier 3+ candidates pending an attack chain.
- **Three Plan 7 drills repeat earlier source families.** `Best Warm Up Ever` (universal opener), `Triangle Setting` (Plans 5–6 source family), and `Cross Court Pepper` (Plan 5 source family) appear unchanged. Repetition raises priority but does not authorize implementation.
- **Plan 7 strengthens the case for an explicit attack-accuracy convention.** Drill 4's 4×4 single-shot box and Drill 6's two-shot-box-per-player geometry are the most concrete BAB evidence so far for how attack targets should be marked on court. They are not interchangeable with Around-the-World's 7-zone ladder; that ladder asks the attacker to hit a sequence of zones, while these drills ask the attacker to repeat a single shot to a fixed accuracy target.
- **Workload is concentrated on attack swings.** Drills 4, 5, 6, and 7 are all swing-volume drills. FIVB's `Spike Exhaustion` and `Continuous Spiking` cautions and the M001 `D77` fatigue-cap policy both apply: any future port must cap total swings, not just successful reps. BAB's "play until +3" language has the same retry-without-cap risk as the Plan 2 serving zones.
- **+3/-3 returns as a scoring wrapper, now applied to attack accuracy.** Plan 2's `Server vs Passer (+3/-3)` scored pass quality; Plan 7 Drill 4 reuses the same +3/-3 cadence to score attack accuracy. Future catalog work should treat +3/-3 as a reusable scoring family across skills, not a serve-receive-only construct.
- **Game-like transition is partially constrained.** Drill 7's "first contact from the north side should be a short attack in front of the line" is a rule-delta over a normal point — closer to FIVB's modified-games shape (`docs/research/fivb-source-material.md` Modified Games chapter; cited in `docs/research/beach-training-resources.md`) than to a standalone drill. Future "pressure block" surface design should keep this rule-delta pattern in mind.

Use this table when deciding whether to add or adapt the Plan 7 drills to `app/src/data/drills.ts`.


| BAB drill                             | Deep read                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Current / future catalog disposition                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Authoring notes if promoted                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| ------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| **Best Warm Up Ever**                 | Repeated source evidence for the universal BAB opener. Plans 1–7 all use it; the opener does not change with focus area.                                                                                                                                                       | Already covered by Plan 1 markup; no new catalog action.                                                                                                                                                                                         | Cite Plans 1–7 if future work needs evidence that BAB treats this as the default opener across passing, setting, and attacking plans.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| **Triangle Setting**                  | Repeated 3-player pass-set-reset triangle from Plans 5 and 6. Plan 7 inserts it as the supporting setting block before attack accuracy work.                                                                                                                                   | Reserved/planned `d43`; deferred under `D101` 3+ player support, not currently authored.                                                                                                                                                         | Same `D101` stance as Plans 5 and 6. Repetition strengthens the source family priority but does not make it pair-native.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| **Cross Court Pepper**                | Repeated 4-player cross-court pepper from Plan 5. Plan 7 uses it as a controlled attack-and-dig rhythm primer before scored attack accuracy work.                                                                                                                              | Future `D101` pepper / game-control candidate. Not current M001 because it requires 4 players, net geometry, blocking/attack roles, and controlled attacking.                                                                                    | `participants.min: 4`; `feedType: partner-toss` to start, then cooperative attack feeds; `needsNet: true`; likely `successMetric.type: streak` or completion. Preserve role labels: "blocking" is positional/role simulation, not necessarily true blocking.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| **+3/-3 Highlines - Cut Shots / HL**  | Three-player single-target attack-accuracy scoring drill: pass → set → attacker shoots for a 4×4 box in the high-line or cut-shot position; +1 in box, -1 miss; play to ±3. Each round trains one shot and one box.                                                            | Tier 3+ attack-chain candidate. Strong source for the attack-accuracy + binary-scoring pairing. Not current M001 because `attack` is not a shipped skill tag and the source form needs 3 players, a net, and marked boxes.                       | `participants.min: 3`; `feedType: live-serve` (or `partner-toss` if "bowls" is preserved) — the source allows either; `needsNet: true`; `needsLines: true` or markers for the 4×4 box; `skillFocus: ['attack']` (with `pass` and `set` declared as supporting); `successMetric.type: points-to-target` matched to the +3/-3 wrapper. Cap **total swings** in addition to ±3 to bound shoulder load (`D77`). Author one variant per shot-target pair (HL, CS) rather than one drill that tries to cover both. |
| **Highlines - Cuts - Open Net Swing** | Four-player open-net swing pattern: passer becomes attacker on the first contact, defender digs to setter on the other side, defender then attacks an **open net** (no blocker). Trains attack from a real pass plus an open-net finish; defender always sits cross-court.     | Tier 3+ open-net attack candidate. Future provenance for an "attack without blocker" sub-family. Not current M001 because it requires 4 players, attack tagging, and explicit blocker-presence metadata.                                         | `participants.min: 4`; `feedType: partner-toss` for the initial feed and live for the dig-to-attack chain; `needsNet: true`; `skillFocus: ['attack']` with `pass`, `set`, `defense` as supporting if/when defense ships. Future drill metadata may need a `blockerPresence` axis (`open` / `blocked`) so open-net drills do not silently get scored against blocked-game expectations. Cap total swings per side.                                                                                            |
| **2 Ball Side Out**                   | Three-player rapid-fire alternating high-line / cut-shot accuracy drill. Both players have their own HL and CS box; each side-out feeds into an immediate scrambled free ball to the partner with the opposite shot target. Targets 5 high lines and 5 cut shots per attacker. | Tier 3+ attack-accuracy + transition candidate. The most courtside-friendly Plan 7 attack drill because the rep count is bounded (5 + 5 per attacker).                                                                                           | `participants.min: 3`; `feedType: partner-toss` (coach role); `needsNet: true`; `needsLines: true` for the box geometry; `skillFocus: ['attack']` with `pass` and `set` supporting; `successMetric.type: reps-successful` capped at 10 per attacker as the source specifies. Box geometry is content-heavy; courtside copy must stay short — defer detailed box-drawing language to a setup-prep card or external diagram, not the run-time card.                                                            |
| **Comp Transition HL - CS - Live**    | Pair-vs-pair competitive sideout with a short-attack rule: receiving team must high-line off the pass; tossing team's defender must attack the dig short (in front of a line 15 ft from the net) before the rally goes live. Alternates 8 rounds, then switches sides.         | Tier 3+ modified-game candidate. Strong source for "rule-delta on a normal point" pressure-block design. Not current M001 because it requires pair-vs-pair (4 players), full-game-play support, attack tagging, and a constraint-rule mechanism. | `participants.min: 4`; `feedType: partner-toss` for the initial toss, then `live-serve`/full-rally; `needsNet: true`; `needsLines: true` for the 15-ft short-attack line; `skillFocus: ['attack']` with `pass`, `set`, `defense` supporting. Track this as a "rule-delta game template" candidate (sibling to FIVB Modified Games) rather than as a fixed-sequence drill. Cap by total rounds (8 per side) as the source specifies; do not let a stuck rally extend the dose.                                |


Implementation consequences:

- **Plan 7 confirms the attack chain is genuinely Tier 3+.** Every novel Plan 7 drill needs at least an `attack` skill tag, a net, marked court boxes, and (in three of four novel drills) 4 players. None of those preconditions exist in M001.
- **Use Plan 7 to anchor the future attack-accuracy box convention.** Drill 4's 4×4 single-shot box and Drill 6's two-shot-per-player box geometry should be cited together when the attack chain is scoped, alongside FIVB 5.6 (5-zone Around-the-World attack) and BAB's own 7-zone attack ladder. The product needs to pick **one** attack-target convention with explicit criteria — these three are not interchangeable.
- **Treat +3/-3 as a cross-skill scoring wrapper, not a serve-receive-only construct.** Plan 2 used it for pass quality; Plan 7 uses it for attack accuracy. Any future pressure-block design should support it generically.
- **Add a `blockerPresence` axis to the future attack metadata wishlist.** Drill 5 is explicitly an open-net drill; later attack drills will pair against a real blocker. Without this axis, the catalog cannot honestly distinguish open-net swing reps from blocked-game swing reps, and progression gating will be misleading.
- **Defer the "short attack" rule (Drill 7) until a rule-delta game-template surface exists.** It is the best Plan 7 evidence for a generic constraint-rule pattern, but importing it as a one-off would entrench it as a fixed drill rather than a reusable template.

### Practice Plan 8 — full text (verbatim founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **second BAB attacking practice plan** captured at source-detail level, and it adds two patterns Plan 7 did not: (1) **technique-level "how to hit X" drills** (Drills 2 and 3) that train per-shot mechanics with a defender-read overlay, and (2) the **rule-restricted variant pattern** (`SHOTS ONLY`, `Round 1 and 2 ONLY`) that subsets earlier drill families to keep practice on the named focus.

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** (15 min): Same universal BAB opener source family captured in Plans 1–7.

- Pass back and forth — 10 each
- Set back and forth — 10 each
- Tomahawk back and forth — 10 each
- Pokey back and forth — 10 each
- Open hand one-handed slap pepper
- Speed pepper — push the speed on the dig, set, and attack
- Defender only: starting from knees to lay-down sprawl dig — 8 each side
- Blocker only: pull digs — 8 each side
- 5 game serves to a passer — pass and catch — each player
- Cross-court dig to a cut shot — setter catches cut shot — 5 each player per side
- Water

**Drill 2 — Hitting a High Line** (10 min): Player 1 is on the south side as the tosser; Players 2 and 3 are on the north side. After tossing, Player 1 should move to the middle of the court, then shift to the cross court to play defense, read the shot, react, dig, and catch the ball.

- Player 1 tosses the ball to Player 2
- Player 2 passes the ball to Player 3
- Player 3 sets the ball back to Player 2
- Player 2 hits a high-line shot

**Drill 3 — Hitting a Cut Shot** (10 min): Player 1 is on the south side as the tosser; Players 2 and 3 are on the north side. After tossing, Player 1 should move to the middle of the court, then shift to the cross court to play defense, read the shot, react, dig, and catch the ball.

- Player 1 tosses the ball to Player 2
- Player 2 passes the ball to Player 3
- Player 3 sets the ball back to Player 2
- Player 2 hits a cut shot

**Drill 4 — Around the World (Toss)** (15 min): Same 7-zone attack-accuracy ladder source family captured in Plan 1. Draw 7 boxes on the court — **Short Poke Line · Mid Line Power · High Line · Deep Middle · Jumbo Cross Court · Hard Angle · Cut Shot**. Each box challenges the attacker to get the ball close to the sideline. A player must hit spot 1 before moving to spot 2; player finishes after all spots. Roles: one tosses, one passes + attacks, one sets. More than 3? Add to the attacking line.

**Drill 5 — Around the World (Serve)** (15 min): Same 7-zone serve-fed sideout-to-attack placement drill source family captured in Plans 1 and 4. Same 7 zones as Drill 4, but with a serve-fed pass instead of a toss. One serves, one passes + attacks, one sets. More than 3? Add to the attacking line.

**Drill 6 — High Line - Cut Shot - Live (only shots)** (15 min): Same competitive transition source family as Plan 7 Drill 7 (`Comp Transition HL - CS - Live`), with the `**(only shots)`** rule restriction. Before starting, draw a line from sideline to sideline on the south side about 15 ft from the net. Players 1 and 2 are Team A on the north side; Players 3 and 4 are Team B on the south side. Team A starts as the tossing team and Team B is receiving. The first attack from the south side should be a high line, and the first contact from the north side should be a short attack in front of the drawn line.

- Team A tosses to Team B
- The Team B player who passes hits a high line
- The defender on Team A runs down and digs the high line from Team B
- The Team A defender attacks the dig so it lands in front of the drawn line on the court
- Finish the play as if it is a live game
- Repeat by tossing to the other Team B player
- Alternate the tosses for 8 rounds, then switch sides of the net with Team A

**Drill 7 — 3 Before 5 (Serve 1 Player) (SHOTS ONLY)** (20–30 min): Same serve-receive pressure source family captured in Plans 1, 3, 4, and 5, with the `**(SHOTS ONLY)`** rule restriction (no hard hits — every attack must be a shot). The serving team serves at the receiving team for the round. The round finishes when either the serving team scores 3 points or the receiving team scores 5 points. Repeat so both teams serve and receive on both sides of the net.

**Drill 8 — Games to 7 - Round 1 and 2 ONLY** (20 min): Same modified-game source family captured in Plan 5 (`Mini Games to 7 (Two Players Battle)`), but with the round set restricted to **Rounds 1 and 2 only** (Cut Shot, then High Line). This drill can be run multiple ways. First decide whether to use a live serve, allowing the server to serve either player, or whether the game is concentrated on one player per game. BAB frames Option 1 as repetition-based game play and Option 2 as competitive reps. Once the option is chosen, play a normal game, but the serving team is assigned a shot that must happen for the first ball. Example rounds: Round 1 Cut Shot, Round 2 High Line, Round 3 Hard Angle, Round 4 Hard Line. Plan 8's restriction is to play only Rounds 1 and 2.

### Practice Plan 8 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 8 is the second attack-focused BAB plan and it complements Plan 7 along two clean axes: (1) it adds the **technique-level foundation** for the per-shot work Plan 7 assumed already existed (`Hitting a High Line`, `Hitting a Cut Shot`), and (2) it introduces a **rule-restricted variant pattern** that subsets existing drills to keep them on the attack focus (`(only shots)`, `(SHOTS ONLY)`, `Round 1 and 2 ONLY`). Plan 8's combination — basic technique drills, the canonical 7-zone Around-the-World ladder (toss + serve), and shot-restricted versions of two prior drills — reads like the **shot-fundamentals counterpart** to Plan 7's shot-accuracy and game-transition emphasis.

Two structural observations matter for future Volleycraft plan-builder work:

- **BAB authors per-shot technique drills as separate records, not as one parameterized drill.** `Hitting a High Line` and `Hitting a Cut Shot` are word-for-word identical except for the named shot. This is the same pattern as `Server vs Passer (Sideline Serves)` vs `(Middle/Seam Serve)` in Plan 2 and the per-shot-target boxes in Plan 7 Drill 4. A future Volleycraft attack chain should preserve the per-shot variant model (one variant per named shot), not collapse all shots into one configurable drill — the tactical claim and the accuracy target differ per shot.
- **Rule-restricted variants are first-class drill rows in BAB, not authoring shortcuts.** Plan 8 lists `(only shots)`, `(SHOTS ONLY)`, and `Round 1 and 2 ONLY` as distinct drills inside the practice flow rather than as runtime toggles on the parent drill. Future Volleycraft authoring should decide whether to model these as: (a) separate drill records, (b) variants on a parent drill, or (c) runtime constraint toggles. Each option has different implications for diagnostics, swap pools, and authoring-budget accounting; the BAB source treats them as (a), but the M001 product may prefer (b) or (c) for catalog parsimony.

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **No new M001 catalog bridge.** Like Plan 7, every novel Plan 8 drill is Tier 3+ pending an attack chain. `Hitting a High Line` and `Hitting a Cut Shot` are the most pair-compatible new drills (3-player source forms), but they still require `attack` skill support, a net, and explicit defender-read mechanics that are not currently expressible.
- **Five Plan 8 drills repeat earlier source families.** `Best Warm Up Ever` (universal opener), `Around the World (Toss)` (Plan 1), `Around the World (Serve)` (Plans 1 and 4), `High Line - Cut Shot - Live (only shots)` (Plan 7 Drill 7 + rule restriction), and `3 Before 5 (Serve 1 Player) (SHOTS ONLY)` (Plans 1/3/4/5 + rule restriction). Repetition strengthens source-family priority but does not authorize implementation.
- `**Hitting a High Line` and `Hitting a Cut Shot` are the missing foundation drills for the Plan 7 shot-accuracy work.** Plan 7 Drill 4 (`+3/-3 Highlines - Cut Shots / HL`) assumed the attacker can already produce the named shot; Plan 8 Drills 2 and 3 train that ability. A future attack chain should likely sequence them as Plan 8 Drills 2/3 → Plan 7 Drill 4, mirroring the BAB ordering.
- **Defender-read overlay is built into the technique drill itself.** Plan 8 explicitly says the tosser becomes a cross-court defender after the toss, reading the shot to dig and catch. Even the basic technique drill is not pure mechanics in BAB; it folds in real defense context. This reinforces Thesis T3 (whole-chain default) in `docs/research/practice-plan-authoring-synthesis.md` — even a "technique" drill returns to the chain.
- `**Around the World (Toss)` is now confirmed verbatim across Plans 1 and 8.** Both list the same 7 zones in the same order. This is strong source-form evidence for the BAB 7-zone attack convention if Volleycraft eventually picks it.
- **The rule-restriction pattern is a constraint-led practice mechanism.** Constraining `3 Before 5` to `SHOTS ONLY` removes hard-hit attacks; constraining `Mini Games to 7` to `Round 1 and 2 ONLY` narrows the shot menu. This is structurally similar to FIVB's modified-games rule deltas (`docs/research/fivb-source-material.md` chapter 8). Future "pressure block" or modified-game surfaces should support this kind of restrictive overlay generically.

Use this table when deciding whether to add or adapt the Plan 8 drills to `app/src/data/drills.ts`.

| -------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |

Plans 1–8 all use it.                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Already covered by Plan 1 markup; no new catalog action.                                                                                                                                                                     | Cite Plans 1–8 if future work needs the strongest evidence yet that BAB treats this as the default opener across all focus areas.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |

The simplest source form for high-line technique. | Tier 3+ attack-chain technique candidate. New drill family — first per-shot technique drill captured in this archive. Not current M001 because `attack` is not a shipped skill tag and the drill needs a net plus 3 players. | `participants.min: 3`; `feedType: partner-toss`; `needsNet: true`; `skillFocus: ['attack']` with `pass`, `set`, and `defense` as supporting if/when defense ships. `successMetric.type: reps-successful` against a "shot lands in court + cross-court area" criterion, not against a marked box (boxes belong to Plan 7 Drill 4 and the +3/-3 wrapper). The per-shot pair is the canonical author-by-shot pattern — when more shot families exist (`Hard Angle`, `Hard Line`, `Jumbo Cross Court`, etc.), each should land as a sibling variant rather than a configurable parameter. Cap total swings per session per shot family (`D77`).                                                                                                                                                    |

Cap total swings per session.                                                                      |

Repetition across Plans 1, 4, and 8 strengthens priority.                                                                                                                       | Same naming-warning as Plans 1 and 4: do not confuse with `d33 Around the World Serving` (the 6-zone serving form). | **High Line - Cut Shot - Live (only shots)** | Rule-restricted variant of Plan 7 Drill 7 (`Comp Transition HL - CS - Live`). Same pair-vs-pair sideout with the 15-ft short-attack line, but the `(only shots)` restriction removes hard-hit attacks.                                                                            | Tier 3+ modified-game variant candidate; sibling to Plan 7 Drill 7.                                                                                                                                                          | If promoted, model the rule restriction as a constraint flag on the parent drill rather than a duplicate record (see "rule-restricted variants" observation above). Source-form participant count (4) and net requirement are unchanged; the only delta is the shot constraint.                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| **3 Before 5 (Serve 1 Player) (SHOTS ONLY)** | Rule-restricted variant of the `3 Before 5` source family (Plans 1, 3, 4, 5).
