The Option 1 vs Option 2 decision (live serve vs concentrated on one player) carries forward from Plan 5 and must be preserved.                                                                                                                                                                                                                               |


Implementation consequences:

- **Plan 8 fills the technique-level gap below Plan 7's accuracy-level work.** The two plans together suggest a future attack chain should sequence: Plan 8 `Hitting X` (technique foundation) → Plan 7 Drills 4–6 (accuracy + open-net) → Plan 7 Drill 7 / Plan 8 Drill 6 (live transition) → Plan 8 Drill 7 (sideout pressure) → Plan 8 Drill 8 (modified game).
- **The rule-restriction pattern (`SHOTS ONLY`, `(only shots)`, `Round N ONLY`) is a generic mechanism, not three one-offs.** Future Volleycraft work should pick **one** modeling approach across the catalog rather than treating each restriction as a unique drill. The cheapest option is a constraint flag on the parent drill; the most explicit option is sibling variant records; the most user-controlled option is a runtime toggle. Each has trade-offs for diagnostics, swap pools, and the authoring-budget cap.
- **Per-shot drills should be sibling variants, not a configurable parent.** BAB's pattern (`Hitting a High Line`, `Hitting a Cut Shot`, the per-shot `+3/-3` boxes in Plan 7 Drill 4, the per-shot rounds in Plan 8 Drill 8) is consistent: one drill per named shot. Volleycraft should follow this for honest tactical claims, not collapse shots into a generic parameter.
- **The 7-zone attack convention is now strongly source-evidenced.** Two verbatim captures (Plans 1 and 8) plus serve-fed appearance in Plans 1 and 4 mean the BAB 7-zone ladder is the most-supported attack-target convention in the captured set. That does not automatically settle the convention question — FIVB's 5-zone version (`docs/research/fivb-source-material.md` Drill 5.6) and BAB's per-shot accuracy boxes (Plan 7 Drill 4) remain valid alternatives — but it raises the BAB 7-zone version's source-authority weight in any future decision.

### Practice Plan 9 — partial source capture (founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **third BAB attacking practice plan** captured at source-detail level. The founder paste captured Drills 2, 3, 4, 5, 7, and 8 in full; Drill 1 (Best Warm Up Ever) is a repeated source family with no new content; Drill 6 (Beat the Blocker Cross/Line) was provided as a name-only entry. Plan 9 introduces the **first observed BAB drill-name aliasing case** — Plan 8 `Hitting a High Line / Cut Shot` and Plan 9 `Offensive Accuracy - HL / CS` are word-for-word identical except for the drill name — plus a **vision/read pepper** drill (`3 Touch Vision Pepper`) and two **competitive game-format** drills (`14-15 Games to 21`, `Set to 21`).

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** *(name only; no captured detail)*: Repeated source family with the universal BAB opener captured in Plans 1–8.

**Drill 2 — 6 Guns** (15 min): Same three-version pepper progression source family captured in Plans 1 and 3. Player 1 and Player 2 face one another as if peppering. The drill is cooperative; the goal across versions is to keep the ball moving with control (Version 1) and speed (Version 2) in a continuous manner. Start with Version 1 and proceed when successfully completed.

- **Version 1**: Speed Pepper using Pass, Set, Hit. Players alternate touches: P1 Pass → P2 Set → P1 Hit → P2 Pass → P1 Set → P2 Hit.
- **Version 2**: Speed Pepper using Tomahawk or Pass. P1 initiates; P2 reacts with pass or tomahawk depending on the ball received. Try to get the ball past the partner with control and speed.
- **Version 3**: Speed Pepper using only one hand. Each partner puts the non-dominant hand behind the back; play legal volleyball touches like forearm digs, pokeys, back-hand flippers, etc. Switch arms after a few successful attempts.

**Drill 3 — 3 Touch Vision Pepper** (10 min): Players 1, 2, and 3 are all on the south side of the net. P1 is on the west sideline; P2 is on the east sideline; P3 sets from the middle of the court.

- P3 tosses a ball to P1
- P1 passes the ball back to P3
- P3 sets the ball back to P1
- P1 hits the ball at P2's hands or platform
- Once the hitter is set, the defender (P2) puts hands up to dig a hard-driven ball overhead **or** leaves hands down to dig a hard-driven ball at the platform; it is the hitter's job to **look** and see what the defender is calling for

**Drill 4 — Offensive Accuracy - HL** (10 min): Same three-player per-shot technique source form as Plan 8 Drill 2 (`Hitting a High Line`); BAB renames the drill in Plan 9 but the source text is identical. P1 is on the south side as the tosser; P2 and P3 are on the north side. After tossing, P1 should move to the middle of the court, then shift to the cross court to play defense, read the shot, react, dig, and catch the ball.

- P1 tosses the ball to P2
- P2 passes the ball to P3
- P3 sets the ball back to P2
- P2 hits a high-line shot

**Drill 5 — Offensive Accuracy - CS** (10 min): Same three-player per-shot technique source form as Plan 8 Drill 3 (`Hitting a Cut Shot`); BAB renames the drill in Plan 9 but the source text is identical. Same setup as Drill 4 above; P2 hits a cut shot.

**Drill 6 — Beat the Blocker Cross/Line** *(name only; no captured detail)*: New drill name not previously catalogued. The name suggests an attack drill that scores attacking past a blocker on either the cross-court or line shot. Re-solicit the source before authoring.

**Drill 7 — Games - 14-15 Games to 21** (30 min): A normal game shortened to ensure good repetition and intensity. The team serving starts with 15. Play a best-of-3/5/7 series depending on time.

**Drill 8 — Set to 21** (20–30 min): A normal set of volleyball. Switch on 7s. Depending on time, play a full match.

### Practice Plan 9 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 9 is the third attack-focused BAB plan and it adds three structural patterns the earlier captures did not surface:

1. **Drill-name aliasing.** Plan 8 `Hitting a High Line` and `Hitting a Cut Shot` reappear in Plan 9 as `Offensive Accuracy - HL` and `Offensive Accuracy - CS` with **identical source text**. This is the first source evidence that BAB drill names are not stable across plans — the same drill can carry two (or more) different names in different practice plans. This is a load-bearing observation for the source-name → our-drill-id cross-reference: a single Volleycraft drill record may need to map to multiple BAB names.
2. **Vision/read attack-pepper drill.** `3 Touch Vision Pepper` introduces a defender-read overlay where the attacker must look at the defender's hand position (up = drive overhead; down = drive at platform) and choose accordingly. This is the first BAB source for an attack-side "look-and-react" drill, and it converges with FIVB's "quick look" cue (already cited from FIVB Drills 3.15 `Pass and Look` and 4.9 `Set and Look`; see `docs/research/beach-training-resources.md` and `docs/research/fivb-source-material.md`).
3. **Competitive-game test formats.** `14-15 Games to 21` and `Set to 21` are normal-game scoring wrappers that test whatever the practice has been working on, rather than training a specific skill. They sit at the most game-like end of the BAB practice arc — beyond pressure scoring drills like `3 Before 5` because there is no shot or focus constraint at all.

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Same Tier 3+ stance for the novel attack work.** `3 Touch Vision Pepper`, `Beat the Blocker Cross/Line`, and the renamed `Offensive Accuracy - HL / CS` all need `attack` skill support, which is not currently shipped. None of them belongs in M001.
- **Five Plan 9 drills repeat earlier source families.** `Best Warm Up Ever` (universal opener), `6 Guns` (Plans 1 and 3 source family), `Offensive Accuracy - HL` ≡ Plan 8 `Hitting a High Line`, `Offensive Accuracy - CS` ≡ Plan 8 `Hitting a Cut Shot`, and `3 Before 5` is implicitly behind several Plan 9 drills (though Drill 7 and Drill 8 are different game formats, not `3 Before 5` variants).
- `**6 Guns` source detail in Plan 9 matches Plan 1 verbatim.** Confirms the three-version pepper progression as a stable BAB source family.
- **The vision/read pattern is stronger evidence for a future `defense_read` or `attack_read` drill subkind than any prior BAB capture.** `3 Touch Vision Pepper` makes the read **the scored decision**, not a coaching cue. If Volleycraft eventually adds attack content, the read-vs-shoot pair (`Hitting a HL` shot mechanics → `3 Touch Vision Pepper` read overlay → `Beat the Blocker` past-blocker placement) is a plausible source-backed progression sequence.
- **The competitive-game drills should not become standalone catalog records.** `Set to 21` and `14-15 Games to 21` are session-shape wrappers, not technique drills. Future Volleycraft work should treat them as session-level constructs (or as "play a game" archetypes), not as drills competing for the authoring-budget cap.

Use this table when deciding whether to add or adapt the Plan 9 drills to `app/src/data/drills.ts`.


| BAB drill                       | Deep read                                                                                                                                                                                   | Current / future catalog disposition                                                                                                                                                                                      | Authoring notes if promoted                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| ------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Best Warm Up Ever**           | Repeated source evidence for the universal BAB opener. Plans 1–9 all use it.                                                                                                                | Already covered by Plan 1 markup; no new catalog action.                                                                                                                                                                  | Cite Plans 1–9 if future work needs the strongest evidence yet that BAB treats this as the default opener across passing, setting, and attacking plans.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| **6 Guns**                      | Repeated source evidence for the three-version pepper progression. Plan 9 source text matches Plan 1 verbatim.                                                                              | Same content-polish candidate as Plan 1.                                                                                                                                                                                  | Repetition across Plans 1, 3, 4, and 9 strengthens priority for a future partner-control / pepper-family drill, but the high-tempo and pair-only constraints remain.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |
| **3 Touch Vision Pepper**       | Three-player attack-pepper drill with a defender-read overlay: P1 attacks at P2 based on whether P2's hands are up or down. The first BAB source for an attack-side "look-and-react" drill. | Tier 3+ attack-chain candidate. New drill family captured at source-detail level for the first time (previously a name-only entry from the Plan 9 TOC). Sibling to FIVB's "quick look" cue and to FIVB Drills 3.15 / 4.9. | `participants.min: 3`; `feedType: partner-toss`; `needsNet: false` (south-side only); `skillFocus: ['attack', 'defense']` if/when defense ships, otherwise treat the read as an attacker-only decision. `successMetric.type` likely `reps-successful` against a "correct read + clean attack" criterion. The vision/read decision is what makes this drill different from straight pepper; do not collapse it into `6 Guns`. |
| **Offensive Accuracy - HL**     | Identical source form to Plan 8 Drill 2 (`Hitting a High Line`); only the drill name differs. First observed BAB drill-name aliasing case.                                                  | Same Tier 3+ per-shot technique candidate as Plan 8 Drill 2. Treat as one catalog drill family with two BAB source names.                                                                                                 | If promoted, model as one drill record (e.g., `Hit a High Line`) with provenance comments citing both BAB source names. The cross-reference table below carries both names mapping to the same future record.                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| **Offensive Accuracy - CS**     | Identical source form to Plan 8 Drill 3 (`Hitting a Cut Shot`); only the drill name differs. Sibling per-shot variant of `Offensive Accuracy - HL`.                                         | Same Tier 3+ per-shot technique candidate as Plan 8 Drill 3. Treat as one catalog drill family with two BAB source names.                                                                                                 | Same modeling approach as `Offensive Accuracy - HL`. Author the per-shot pair as sibling variants, not as a configurable parent (per Thesis T8 in `docs/research/practice-plan-authoring-synthesis.md`).                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| **Beat the Blocker Cross/Line** | Source detail not captured. Drill name implies an attack drill scored on placing the attack past a blocker on either the cross-court or line shot.                                          | Tier 3+ attack-chain candidate; partial capture. Re-solicit source before authoring.                                                                                                                                      | Expected source constraints when re-solicited: `participants.min: 3` or 4 (attacker, setter, blocker, possibly defender); `feedType: partner-toss`; `needsNet: true`; `skillFocus: ['attack']`. Likely future provenance for a `blockerPresence: 'blocked'` attack drill, complementing Plan 7 Drill 5's `Open Net Swing` (`blockerPresence: 'open'`).                                                                       |
| **Games - 14-15 Games to 21**   | Competitive game-format drill: a normal game with the serving team starting at 15, played as best-of-3/5/7. Tests whatever the practice has been working on; not a technique drill.         | Tier 3+ session-wrapper candidate. Should not become a standalone catalog drill record.                                                                                                                                   | If exposed at all, treat as a session archetype or a "play a game" surface element, not as a row in `app/src/data/drills.ts`. The compressed-score format reduces total swings/serves vs a full game; a future workload-aware game wrapper should preserve that property.                                                                                                                                                    |
| **Set to 21**                   | Competitive game-format drill: a normal set with side switches at 7s; play a full match if time allows.                                                                                     | Tier 3+ session-wrapper candidate. Should not become a standalone catalog drill record.                                                                                                                                   | Same modeling guidance as `14-15 Games to 21`. The full-set length is the most game-realistic of the BAB-captured competitive wrappers; future authoring should cap by total swings/serves and stop on technique drop, not by score alone (`D77`).                                                                                                                                                                           |


Implementation consequences:

- **Cross-reference table needs a "drill-name aliases" mechanism.** With Plan 9, the source-name → app-drill-id mapping is no longer one-to-one. Future BAB captures may surface more name aliases; the table now records both Plan 8 and Plan 9 names for the per-shot technique drills as aliases of one future drill family.
- `**3 Touch Vision Pepper` is the strongest BAB evidence so far for an attack-read drill subkind.** When the attack chain is scoped, sequence it after the per-shot technique drills (`Hitting a HL / CS` ≡ `Offensive Accuracy - HL / CS`) and before the past-blocker drills (`Beat the Blocker Cross/Line`). FIVB's 3.15 / 4.9 "Look" drills can be cited alongside it for cross-source convergence.
- `**Beat the Blocker Cross/Line` cannot be authored from the Plan 9 capture alone.** Re-solicit the source. When acquired, evaluate as the blocked-attack counterpart to Plan 7 Drill 5's open-net swing, supporting the proposed `blockerPresence` axis.
- **Don't catalog `14-15 Games to 21` or `Set to 21` as drill records.** They are session-shape wrappers and belong in archetype/session-template territory, not in `drills.ts`. Rolling them into the catalog as drills would inflate the authoring-budget cap with rows that the runtime can't honestly score per-rep.

### Practice Plan 10 — partial source capture (founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **fourth BAB attacking practice plan** captured at source-detail level. Drill 1 (Best Warm Up Ever) is name-only; Drills 2–9 are captured in full. Plan 10 is the densest attack-plan capture so far for new structural patterns: a **fourth Triangle Setting source form** (4-player hit-fed with a level-scaled continuous-vs-catch rule), the **Serve to Free Ball** sideout-to-transition pattern, a **defender-role-differentiated drill family** (Drills 4–7) where the same skeleton varies by attacker shot, blocker position, and defender pickup zone, and **two more drill-name aliasing cases** (Plan 10 Drill 8 ≡ Plan 7 Drill 7; Plan 10 Drill 9 ≡ Plan 9 Drill 7).

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** *(name only; no captured detail)*: Repeated source family with the universal BAB opener captured in Plans 1–9.

**Drill 2 — Triangle Setting** (10–20 min): A **fourth Triangle Setting source form**, distinct from the 3-player versions in Plans 5/7 and from the 4-player serve-fed version in Plan 6 Drill 4. P1 is on the net in front of the left-side player. P2 is in the court in the passing position. P3 and P4 are on the right side of the court, **alternating to set**. P1 hits the ball at P2 10 times; P2 passes; P3 and P4 set back to P1.

- **Beginners** should catch after the set
- **Intermediate / Advanced** should try to make the drill continuous by hitting the set back to the passer
- Each round, every player gets to pass and set 10 balls each, then switch sides

This is the first BAB source captured with **explicit per-level rule deltas inside a single drill description** — the drill changes shape by level rather than scaling a parameter.

**Drill 3 — Serve to Free Ball** (10–20 min): Team A is on the south side; Team B is on the north side. Trains both serve-receive sideout and free-ball transition reception in one drill.

- Team A serves a ball to one player on Team B; that player passes, sets, and hits
- After the player hits the ball, the second player on Team A tosses a free ball to the **other player on Team B** (the one who didn't pass), allowing them to pass, set, and hit
- Repeat so each player receives 4 serves and 4 free balls
- Once each person has completed their amount of reps, switch so both teams get to go

This is the first BAB source captured for a **sideout → free-ball transition chain** as a deliberate drill — free-ball reception is a different skill from serve reception, and Plan 10 makes that explicit.

**Drill 4 — High Line from a Serve with Defense** (15 min): Team A serves to the left-side player of Team B. The left-side player receives 10 serves from Team A (5 from each player) and must hit 10 high lines. The defense on the other side plays normal defense, working on picking up a cut shot. If a dig is made, the setter/blocker should catch to keep the drill moving. Complete the drill by serving every player on their desired side of the court.

**Drill 5 — Cut Shot from a Serve with Defense, Blocker Blocking Line** (no time captured; same shape as Drill 4): Team A serves to the left-side player of Team B. The left-side player receives 10 serves (5 from each player) and must hit 10 cut shots. **Blocker blocks line; defender picks up the cut shot.** If a dig is made, catch to keep the drill moving.

**Drill 6 — Cut Shot from a Serve with Defense, Blocker Blocking Cross** (no time captured): Same shape as Drills 4 and 5 but with a **different blocker position and defender pickup zone**. Left-side player receives 10 serves and must hit 10 cut shots / cross-court hits over the block. **Blocker blocks cross; defender picks up the highline.** If a dig is made, catch to keep the drill moving.

**Drill 7 — Hard Cross from a Serve with Defense** (no time captured): Same shape as Drills 4–6. Left-side player receives 10 serves and must hit 10 hard-cross attacks. **Defense plays normal defense, working on picking up a hard attack.** If a dig is made, catch to keep the drill moving.

**Drill 8 — Competitive - HL - CS - To Live Play** (20 min): **Same source form as Plan 7 Drill 7 (`Comp Transition HL - CS - Live`)** with a different drill name. Before starting, draw a line from sideline to sideline on the south side about 15 ft from the net. Players 1 and 2 are Team A on the north side; Players 3 and 4 are Team B on the south side. Team A starts as the tossing team and Team B is receiving. The first attack from the south side should be a high line, and the first contact from the north side should be a short attack in front of the drawn line.

- Team A tosses to Team B
- The Team B player who passes hits a high line
- The defender on Team A runs down and digs the high line from Team B
- The Team A defender attacks the dig so it lands in front of the drawn line on the court
- Finish the play as if it is a live game
- Repeat by tossing to the other Team B player
- Alternate the tosses for 8 rounds, then switch sides of the net with Team A

**Drill 9 — 14-15 Games to 21, Best of 3** (remaining time): **Same source form as Plan 9 Drill 7 (`Games - 14-15 Games to 21`)** with a different drill name. A normal game shortened to ensure good repetition and intensity. The team serving starts with 15. Play a best-of-3/5/7 series depending on time. The Plan 10 title's "Best of 3" parameter matches the Plan 9 source text's "best of 3/5/7" framing.

### Practice Plan 10 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 10 is the fourth attack-focused BAB plan and it is structurally the **defender-aware attack** plan. Where Plan 7 trained shot accuracy without a real defender (or with a defender sitting in a fixed position), Plan 8 trained shot technique with a passive defender-read overlay, and Plan 9 added vision/read pepper, Plan 10 puts the **full pair-vs-pair defensive shape** behind every novel drill. Drills 4–7 are a four-cell matrix:


| Drill | Attacker named shot         | Blocker position | Defender pickup zone                   |
| ----- | --------------------------- | ---------------- | -------------------------------------- |
| 4     | High Line                   | (not specified)  | Cut shot                               |
| 5     | Cut Shot                    | Line             | Cut shot (because blocker takes line)  |
| 6     | Cut Shot / Cross over block | Cross            | Highline (because blocker takes cross) |
| 7     | Hard Cross                  | (not specified)  | Hard attack                            |


This matrix is a structurally important source pattern. Future Volleycraft attack content needs to express:

- **Attacker named shot** (HL, CS, hard cross, hard angle, hard line, etc.)
- **Blocker position** (line, cross, none, or "open net")
- **Defender pickup zone** (cut shot, highline, hard attack)
- **Coupling rule** between blocker position and defender pickup (when the blocker takes line, the defender takes the cut shot; when the blocker takes cross, the defender takes the highline)

The BAB Drill 6 wording — "blocker blocks cross; defender picks up the highline" — is the cleanest source for this **blocker-defender pairing rule**. It is the beach-defense equivalent of the moving-triangle passing theory: defender position is **relative to the blocker**, not absolute. This is significant for future `attack` and `defense` skill authoring because most existing M001 metadata cannot express blocker-defender coupling honestly.

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Same Tier 3+ stance for the novel attack and defense work.** All Plan 10 novel drills require pair-vs-pair (4 players), `attack` skill support, and at least the `blockerPresence` axis from Plan 7's open-net swing — none of those exist in M001.
- **Plan 10 introduces level-scaled rules within a single drill.** The Triangle Setting (4-player hit-fed) variant explicitly says "Beginners catch / Intermediate-Advanced continuous." This is a different mechanism from Plan 2's per-level zone scaling (which was a config parameter): Plan 10 changes the **drill behavior** by level. Future Volleycraft authoring should decide whether per-level rules live as variants, as runtime difficulty toggles, or as authored `progression` / `regression` references between drill records.
- `**Serve to Free Ball` is the first BAB source for a sideout-to-free-ball transition drill.** Free-ball reception is a different skill from serve reception (different trajectory, different decision pace, different setter expectation). Future Volleycraft content should not silently treat them as the same.
- **Two more drill-name aliasing cases.** Plan 10 Drill 8 ≡ Plan 7 Drill 7 (`Competitive - HL - CS - To Live Play` ≡ `Comp Transition HL - CS - Live`); Plan 10 Drill 9 ≡ Plan 9 Drill 7 (`14-15 Games to 21, Best of 3` ≡ `Games - 14-15 Games to 21`). Combined with the Plan 8 / Plan 9 per-shot rename, BAB now shows three separate aliasing cases. The cross-reference table is multi-name aware, but the alias mechanism should be formalized before the attack chain ships.
- **A fourth Triangle Setting source form joins the family.** There are now four distinct Triangle Setting source forms in the captured set:
  - Plan 5 / Plan 7 Triangle Setting: 3-player, P1 toss-or-hit feeds, basic
  - Plan 6 Triangle Setting: 3-player, repeated source family from Plan 5
  - Plan 6 Triangle Setting (Serve/Toss): 4-player, serve-fed
  - Plan 6 Triangle Setting Off Serve - Off Pass: 4-player, off-pass correction
  - Plan 6 Triangle Setting Off Serve - Run Through Back Sets: 4-player, advanced correction
  - Plan 10 Triangle Setting: 4-player, hit-fed, with level-scaled continuous-vs-catch rule
  - All carry the same BAB name. Future Volleycraft authoring needs explicit naming discipline (e.g., `Triangle Setting (3p toss)`, `Triangle Setting (4p hit-fed)`) to avoid catalog confusion.

Use this table when deciding whether to add or adapt the Plan 10 drills to `app/src/data/drills.ts`.


| BAB drill                                                      | Deep read                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Current / future catalog disposition                                                                                                                                                                   | Authoring notes if promoted                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| -------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| **Best Warm Up Ever**                                          | Repeated source evidence for the universal BAB opener. Plans 1–10 all use it.                                                                                                                                                       | Already covered by Plan 1 markup; no new catalog action.                                                                                                                                               | Cite Plans 1–10 if future work needs the strongest evidence yet that BAB treats this as the default opener across passing, setting, and attacking plans.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| **Triangle Setting (4-player hit-fed)**                        | Fourth distinct Triangle Setting source form. P1 hits at P2 (passer); P3 and P4 alternate setting back to P1. Beginners catch after the set; Intermediate/Advanced make the drill continuous by hitting the set back to the passer. | Tier 3+ candidate distinct from `d43` (3-player) and the Plan 6 4-player serve-fed source form. Future provenance for a hit-fed setter-rotation drill.                                                 | `participants.min: 4`; `feedType: partner-toss` or `coach-hit`; `needsNet: true`; `skillFocus: ['set']` with `pass`, `attack`, `defense` as supporting; level-scaled rule needs an explicit modeling decision (variants vs runtime toggle vs progression/regression links). Author with disambiguating name to avoid collision with the 3-player Triangle Setting. Cap reps at 10 per role per side as the source specifies.    |
| **Serve to Free Ball**                                         | Pair-vs-pair sideout chain followed by a free-ball transition chain to the **other** player. Each player receives 4 serves + 4 free balls. Trains serve reception, free-ball reception, sideout, and transition in one drill.       | Tier 3+ candidate; new drill family for sideout-to-transition chains.                                                                                                                                  | `participants.min: 4`; `feedType: live-serve` for the first chain and `partner-toss` for the free ball; `needsNet: true`; `skillFocus: ['attack']` with `pass`, `set`, and free-ball-reception (potentially a new variant under `pass`) as supporting. Cap by serves + free balls (8 per player) and total swings. Free-ball reception is a different skill claim from serve reception — keep them distinct in `successMetric`. |
| **High Line from a Serve with Defense**                        | Pair-vs-pair drill: receiver hits 10 high lines off serve; defense picks up the cut shot; setter/blocker catches digs to keep the drill moving.                                                                                     | Tier 3+ candidate; first BAB source for the defender-role-differentiated attack matrix (Drills 4–7).                                                                                                   | `participants.min: 4`; `feedType: live-serve`; `needsNet: true`; `skillFocus: ['attack']` with `pass`, `set`, `defense` supporting. The 10-serves-per-receiver dose is consistent with `D77` fatigue caps; cap total swings across the 4-drill matrix when designing a session. Author as one variant in the Drills 4–7 family rather than a standalone record.                                                                 |
| **Cut Shot from a Serve with Defense, Blocker Blocking Line**  | Same skeleton as Drill 4; receiver hits cut shots; blocker blocks line; defender picks up cut shot.                                                                                                                                 | Tier 3+ candidate; sibling variant in the Drills 4–7 matrix.                                                                                                                                           | Same authoring notes as Drill 4. The `blockerPresence: 'blocked'` + `blockerPosition: 'line'` axis pair needs to be expressible in metadata.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| **Cut Shot from a Serve with Defense, Blocker Blocking Cross** | Same skeleton as Drills 4–5; receiver hits cut shots / cross over the block; **blocker blocks cross; defender picks up highline.** Inverse blocker-defender coupling from Drill 5.                                                  | Tier 3+ candidate; sibling variant in the Drills 4–7 matrix; cleanest source for the blocker-defender coupling rule.                                                                                   | Same authoring notes as Drill 4. `blockerPosition: 'cross'`. The Drill 5 / Drill 6 contrast is the load-bearing source for "defender position is relative to the blocker, not absolute."                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| **Hard Cross from a Serve with Defense**                       | Same skeleton as Drills 4–6; receiver hits hard cross; defense picks up hard attack.                                                                                                                                                | Tier 3+ candidate; sibling variant in the Drills 4–7 matrix; introduces a hard-hit attack variant alongside the shot variants.                                                                         | Same authoring notes as Drill 4. Hard-hit attacks may need a separate `successMetric` than shot drills (placement matters less; pace/timing matters more). Cap total hard-hit reps separately from shot reps because shoulder load is higher.                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| **Competitive - HL - CS - To Live Play**                       | Same source form as Plan 7 Drill 7 (`Comp Transition HL - CS - Live`); third drill-name aliasing case in BAB.                                                                                                                       | Tier 3+ candidate; one drill family with two source names (`Comp Transition HL - CS - Live` ≡ `Competitive - HL - CS - To Live Play`); the Plan 8 `(only shots)` variant is a rule-restricted sibling. | Treat as one record with multiple BAB names in provenance comments. The cross-reference table now lists both names mapping to the same future drill family.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| **14-15 Games to 21, Best of 3**                               | Same source form as Plan 9 Drill 7 (`Games - 14-15 Games to 21`); fourth drill-name aliasing case in BAB.                                                                                                                           | Tier 3+ session-wrapper candidate. Should not become a standalone catalog drill record.                                                                                                                | Treat as one session-wrapper construct with multiple BAB names. The "Best of 3" parameter matches the Plan 9 "best of 3/5/7" framing — the Plan 10 title locks one specific best-of value.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |


Implementation consequences:

- **The defender-role-differentiated attack matrix (Drills 4–7) is the strongest BAB source so far for blocker-defender coupling.** Future Volleycraft attack/defense content needs metadata for blocker position, defender pickup zone, and the coupling rule. Treat the four drills as one drill family with sibling variants, not four separate records.
- **The fourth Triangle Setting source form requires naming discipline.** With four distinct `Triangle Setting` source forms now captured, future authoring should disambiguate explicitly (e.g., `Triangle Setting (3p toss)`, `Triangle Setting (3p hit)`, `Triangle Setting (4p serve)`, `Triangle Setting (4p hit-fed)`) rather than rely on plan number to disambiguate.
- `**Serve to Free Ball` argues for separating serve reception from free-ball reception in `pass` skill metadata.** They are different perception-action problems (different trajectory, decision pace, setter expectation). The catalog probably needs a `feedType: 'live-serve' | 'free-ball'` distinction (or similar) before this drill can land honestly.
- **Level-scaled rules within a single drill description need a modeling decision.** Plan 10 Triangle Setting changes drill behavior by level (catch vs continuous). Volleycraft can model this as separate variants, runtime difficulty toggles, or `progression` / `regression` links between two records. The choice should align with the T8 / T9 modeling decisions for per-shot variants and rule-restricted variants — same authoring philosophy across the catalog.
- **Drill-name aliasing is now a recurring pattern, not a one-off.** Three confirmed aliasing cases (per-shot HL/CS, Comp Transition, 14-15 Games) plus a likely fourth (Plan 10 Drill 4–7's relationship to FIVB and earlier BAB sideout drills) mean the cross-reference table format should be formalized to record aliases explicitly before the attack chain ships.

### Practice Plan 11 — partial source capture (founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **fifth BAB attacking practice plan** captured at source-detail level. Drill 1 (Best Warm Up Ever) is name-only; Drills 2–7 are captured in full. Plan 11's most important contribution is **the full source text for `Beat the Blocker`**, which had been a name-only entry from Plan 9 Drill 6. Plan 11 also introduces a **rule-augmented variant** of Plan 7 Drill 4's `+3/-3 Highlines` (blocker-touch penalty added — sibling but inverse to Plan 8's rule-restricted variants) and adds another `14-15 Games to 21` best-of parameter case (Plan 11 = best of 5; Plan 10 = best of 3). Drills 2 (Triangle Setting 4-player hit-fed) and 3 (Cross Court Pepper) are repeated source families with text identical to earlier captures.

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** *(name only; no captured detail)*: Repeated source family with the universal BAB opener captured in Plans 1–10.

**Drill 2 — Triangle Setting** (10–20 min): Same 4-player hit-fed Triangle Setting source form captured in Plan 10 Drill 2 (the **fourth Triangle Setting source form**). Source text identical to Plan 10. P1 is on the net in front of the left-side player; P2 is in the court in the passing position; P3 and P4 are on the right side, alternating to set. P1 hits at P2 10 times; P2 passes; P3/P4 set back to P1. Beginners catch after the set; Intermediate/Advanced make the drill continuous by hitting the set back to the passer. Each round 10 reps per role; switch sides.

**Drill 3 — Cross Court Pepper** (10 min): Same 4-player cross-court pepper source family captured in Plans 5 and 7. Source text identical. Players 1 and 2 on north (NW, NE), Players 3 and 4 on south (SE, SW). Round 1: Players 2 and 4 dig and attack while Players 1 and 3 are "blocking" and setting. Each side gets three touches: pass, set, controlled attack. Continue for a rep count or back-and-forth goal, then switch roles.

**Drill 4 — +3/-3 Highlines (CS / HL with Blocker)** (30 min): Rule-augmented variant of Plan 7 Drill 4 (`+3/-3 Highlines - Cut Shots / HL`). Same setup as Plan 7 (P1 south as tosser/server; P2 and P3 north; 4×4 box drawn in HL or CS location), with **one new scoring rule**: if the blocker touches the ball, the attacker loses 1 point.

- P1 bowls or serves the ball to P2
- P2 passes to P3
- P3 sets P2
- P2 shoots for the high-line or cut-shot box; +1 in box, -1 miss; play to ±3
- **New rule:** if the blocker touches the ball, it is -1

The blocker is implicitly P3 (or whichever north-side player is not setting), inserted as a passive defensive presence whose touch counts against the attacker. This makes the drill a **rule-augmented** sibling to Plan 8's rule-**restricted** variants — Plan 8 narrows the parent drill (`SHOTS ONLY`); Plan 11 extends the parent drill (blocker-touch penalty). Both are constraint overlays on a parent, but the intent differs.

**Drill 5 — Beat the Blocker** (20 min): Full source text for the drill that was name-only in Plan 9 Drill 6 (`Beat the Blocker Cross/Line`). Team A is on the north side; Team B is on the south side. Team A receives 10 balls (5 per player) and must hit a hard-driven shot back at Team B challenging the blocker. **Two big squares are drawn on the Line and in the Angle.** The blocker either grabs the ball, blocks line, or blocks cross. The attacker must see the blocker and either challenge them (swing at the block) or swing away (around the block). **It is okay to get blocked in the drill — that shows the blocker has good form.** Each player gets multiple swings and blocks.

This is the **blocked-attack analog to Plan 7 Drill 5's `Open Net Swing`** and the most explicit BAB source for an attack drill where the attacker reads a real blocker and chooses to challenge or avoid. It complements `3 Touch Vision Pepper` (Plan 9 Drill 3, which reads defender hand position) and the Plan 10 Drills 4–7 matrix (which fixes the blocker-defender pair). Plan 11 Drill 5 is the version where the attacker **chooses** what to do against the blocker, rather than being told a named shot.

**Drill 6 — 14-15 Games to 21, Best of 5** (30 min): Same competitive game-format wrapper source family as Plan 9 Drill 7 (`Games - 14-15 Games to 21`) and Plan 10 Drill 9 (`14-15 Games to 21, Best of 3`), with the best-of parameter set to **5** instead of 3. Source text framing matches: serving team starts at 15; play a best-of 3/5/7 series depending on time. Plan 11's title locks "Best of 5" as the specific value.

**Drill 7 — Set to 21** (remainder of practice): Same source family as Plan 9 Drill 8 with a shorter description ("Normal set to 21"). The Plan 9 capture has the longer description (switch on 7s; play a full match if time allows); Plan 11 collapses it to the canonical name. Source form unchanged. *(The founder paste shows "Drive 7" as a typo for "Drill 7"; archive captures the canonical "Drill 7".)*

### Practice Plan 11 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 11 is the fifth attack-focused BAB plan and it is structurally a **read-the-blocker** plan. Where Plan 7 trained shot accuracy without a real blocker (or with the blocker as a fixed obstacle in the +3/-3 box drill), Plan 8 trained shot technique with no blocker, Plan 9 added vision/read pepper against a defender, and Plan 10 fixed the blocker-defender pair in a four-cell matrix, **Plan 11 makes the blocker a reactive presence the attacker must read in real time** (Drill 5 `Beat the Blocker`) and adds a blocker-touch penalty to the +3/-3 accuracy drill (Drill 4) so the attacker has to compute around the blocker even on shot work.

Three structural observations matter for future Volleycraft plan-builder work:

1. **Plan 11 supplies the missing source detail for `Beat the Blocker`.** The Plan 9 cross-reference row for `Beat the Blocker Cross/Line` was previously flagged as needing re-solicitation. Plan 11 Drill 5 closes that gap: the drill is a 4-player hard-hit attack drill where the blocker has three modes (grab / block line / block cross) and the attacker reads to either challenge or avoid. The two big squares "drawn on the Line and in the Angle" are the scoring targets — separate from Plan 7's HL/CS accuracy boxes (which are placement-only) because here the attacker hits hard, not finesse.
2. **Rule-augmented variants are the inverse of rule-restricted variants.** Plan 8 introduced rule restriction (`(SHOTS ONLY)`, `Round N ONLY`) — the variant subsets the parent drill's behavior. Plan 11 Drill 4 introduces rule augmentation — the variant adds a new scoring rule (blocker-touch penalty) to the parent drill's behavior. Both are constraint overlays on a parent, and both fall under Thesis T9 in `docs/research/practice-plan-authoring-synthesis.md`. The same modeling decision applies (separate records / sibling variants / runtime toggles), but T9 should be sharpened to acknowledge augmentation as a sibling pattern to restriction.
3. `**Beat the Blocker` extends Thesis T11 (defender-blocker coupling).** Plan 10 Drills 4–7 are the strongest source for the blocker-defender pair as a fixed unit. Plan 11 Drill 5 extends T11 with a different scenario: the **blocker chooses**, and the attacker reads the blocker. The defender role is implicit (the rest of Team B picks up what the attacker hits past the block). Future Volleycraft attack content needs both: fixed-blocker drills (Plan 10) and reactive-blocker drills (Plan 11). The `blockerPosition` axis from T11 needs an extra value for "reactive" (or a separate axis for blocker behavior, choosing among grab / line / cross).

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Same Tier 3+ stance for all Plan 11 novel work.** `attack` is not a shipped `SkillFocus`, blocker-presence axes are not in metadata, and there are no current 4-player drills in `app/src/data/drills.ts`. None of Plan 11's novel content is M001-eligible.
- **Two Plan 11 drills repeat earlier source families verbatim.** `Triangle Setting` (Plan 10 Drill 2) and `Cross Court Pepper` (Plans 5 and 7). Repetition strengthens source-family priority but does not authorize implementation.
- `**Beat the Blocker` is now ready for authoring (when attack chain activates).** The Plan 9 cross-reference row's "re-solicit before authoring" caveat is closed. Future Volleycraft work can cite Plan 11 Drill 5 as the canonical source. Note: Plan 9 calls it `Beat the Blocker Cross/Line`; Plan 11 calls it just `Beat the Blocker` — another mild aliasing case.
- **The `+3/-3` scoring wrapper now has three documented variants:** Plan 2 `Server vs Passer (+3/-3)` (pass quality), Plan 7 `+3/-3 Highlines - Cut Shots` (attack accuracy, no blocker), and Plan 11 `+3/-3 Highlines (CS / HL with Blocker)` (attack accuracy with blocker-touch penalty). Future cross-skill `+3/-3` modeling needs to support augmentations like blocker-touch -1.
- **Hard-hit attacks need separate workload accounting from shot attacks.** Plan 11 Drill 5 explicitly says "hard-driven shot," not finesse. FIVB's `Spike Exhaustion` and `Continuous Spiking` cautions plus `D77` fatigue caps argue for capping hard-hit reps separately. The Plan 11 dose (10 balls per player, 5 per server) is consistent with `D77`-style dosing.
- **Plan 11 Drill 4's blocker-touch -1 rule has a re-think implication for Plan 7 Drill 4.** Plan 7 Drill 4 had no blocker; Plan 11 Drill 4 adds one. If Volleycraft eventually authors `+3/-3 HL/CS`, the blocker presence should be a sibling-variant axis (no blocker / passive blocker / reactive blocker) rather than a runtime toggle, because the scoring rule changes meaningfully across the three.

Use this table when deciding whether to add or adapt the Plan 11 drills to `app/src/data/drills.ts`.

Implementation consequences:

- `**Beat the Blocker` is now authoring-ready when the attack chain activates.** The Plan 9 cross-reference row's re-solicitation caveat closes; future authoring can cite Plan 11 Drill 5 as canonical source.
- **Rule-augmented variants are a sibling pattern to rule-restricted variants under Thesis T9.** Plan 8 narrowed parent drills (`SHOTS ONLY`); Plan 11 Drill 4 augments parent drills (blocker-touch -1). Both are constraint overlays. T9's modeling decision (separate records / sibling variants / runtime toggles) should support both patterns symmetrically — if runtime toggles are chosen, the toggle system needs to express both restriction and augmentation cleanly.
- **The `blockerPosition` / `blockerPresence` schema axis needs an additional value or a separate behavior axis for reactive blockers.** Plan 10's matrix has `'line' | 'cross'` (fixed); Plan 11 Drill 5 needs `'reactive'` (chooses among grab / line / cross). Either extend `blockerPosition` with a `'reactive'` value or add a separate `blockerBehavior: 'fixed' | 'reactive'` axis. The latter is cleaner because reactive blockers cycle through positions during the drill.
- **The `+3/-3` cross-skill scoring wrapper now has three documented variants.** Plan 2 (pass quality), Plan 7 (attack accuracy, no blocker), Plan 11 (attack accuracy, passive blocker with -1 penalty). Future generic `+3/-3` modeling should support all three through configurable scoring rules, not three separate drill records.

### Practice Plan 12 — partial source capture (founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **first BAB defensive practice plan** captured at source-detail level — earlier captures were passing (Plans 1–4), setting (Plans 5–6), and attacking (Plans 7–11). Plan 12 begins the captured Defensive cluster (Plans 12–16) and supplies two pieces that the earlier captures did not have: a **per-shot defensive technique drill** (`Partner Toss Dig to Cut Shot`, the dig-side analog of Plan 8's `Hitting a HL / CS`) and the full source for `4 Steps to Paradise` (a defensive-movement drill that previously existed only as a name-only cross-reference entry). Three Plan 12 drills are repeats of earlier captures with different drill names, exposing three more drill-name aliasing cases.

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** *(name only; no captured detail)*: Repeated source family with the universal BAB opener captured in Plans 1–11.

**Drill 2 — Partner Toss Dig to Cut Shot** (10–20 min): Players 1 and 2 are both on the south side of the court. P1 is at the starting position for digging a hard-angle attack. P2 is at the net acting as the attacker, tossing a "cut shot" for the defender to dig. P1 uses **one crossover step and a laydown/dive** to get to the ball. **At contact, lift the dig to antenna height.** First round, dig as if defending a left-side cut shot; then switch to digging a cut shot for the right side.

This is the **first per-shot defensive technique drill** captured in this archive — the dig-side analog of Plan 8 Drills 2 / 3 (`Hitting a High Line / Cut Shot`) and Plan 9 Drills 4 / 5 (`Offensive Accuracy - HL / CS`). The structural pattern is identical: one drill per named shot, with the partner acting as a passive feeder so the focus stays on the named technique. Plan 12 captures only the cut-shot version; future captures may surface the high-line-dig sibling.

**Drill 3 — 4 Steps to Paradise** (10–20 min): Players 1, 2, and 3 are all on the south side of the net. P1 is on the court facing the net. P2 and P3 are at each antenna facing the endline's diagonal corner. P1 works on digging the ball in the **cross-court defense position** ("Paradise") looking at the diagonal hitter, then completes a **4-step process** to get to the next digging spot. The steps are **crossover, step, plant, plant**.

This is the canonical drill where the "Paradise" term comes from (Paradise = the cross-court defense position you want to be in as a defender). The drill trains **defensive movement between digging positions** — specifically, the footwork to transition from one cross-court defense position to the next when the attack rotates sides. The 4-step sequence (crossover → step → plant → plant) is BAB's prescribed footwork pattern, structurally similar to setting footwork's off-foot/net-foot sequence (Plan 5 Drill 2) but for defense.

**Drill 4 — Serve a Spot - Dig Set Hit** *(no time captured)*: **Same source form as Plan 2 Drill 4 (`Serve Spot, Dig Set Hit`)** with a different drill name. Source text matches: draw two lines from end line to net about 5 ft from the sidelines; P1 north, P2 south; P2 serves to the northwest zone, then gets to defensive position; P1 tosses or hits a high-line or cut-shot for P2 to dig; P2 digs, sets self, looks at P1's directional point (east or west), and hits to the called zone; switch jobs after reps; switch from northwest to northeast serving target after each round.

This drill appears in two different focus areas: Plan 2 frames it as a passing/serving plan drill; Plan 12 reframes it for defensive emphasis (the dig is now the focus skill, not the pass). The drill itself is unchanged. This is the first captured BAB evidence of **drill-repurposing across focus areas** — the same physical drill is run inside multiple practice contexts, with different focus framing per plan.

**Drill 5 — Competitive - HL - CS - to Live Play** (20 min): **Same source form as Plan 7 Drill 7 (`Comp Transition HL - CS - Live`) and Plan 10 Drill 8 (`Competitive - HL - CS - To Live Play`)**. Source text matches all three. Plan 12 extends the existing alias chain to three plans for the same competitive transition drill. The Plan 12 title differs from Plan 10 only by lowercase "to" instead of capitalized "To".

**Drill 6 — Mini Games to 7 (First Ball Focused Shot)** (20 min): **Same source form as Plan 5 Drill 8 (`Mini Games to 7 (Two Players Battle) (Option 1)`)** with a different parenthetical name. Source text matches: live-serve vs concentrated-on-one-player options; team serving is given a first-ball shot constraint; example rounds Cut Shot / High Line / Hard Angle / Hard Line. The Plan 5 parenthetical (`Two Players Battle (Option 1)`) frames the drill as a competitive battle; the Plan 12 parenthetical (`First Ball Focused Shot`) names the constraint mechanism. Both are the same drill source form.

**Drill 7 — 14-15 Games to 21, Best of 5** (remainder of practice): **Same source form as Plan 11 Drill 6 (`14-15 Games to 21, Best of 5`)**. Source text matches verbatim, including the same "Best of 5" parameter locking.

### Practice Plan 12 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 12 is the first defense-focused BAB plan and it is structurally a **defense-grammar opening capture**. Where Plan 7 set the attack grammar (technique → accuracy → game-transition), Plan 12 begins the defense grammar with three observable building blocks: **per-shot dig technique** (Drill 2), **defensive movement between positions** (Drill 3), and **integrated defense in a sideout chain** (Drill 4). Drills 5–7 are competitive wrappers borrowed from earlier focus areas — confirming that BAB closes most plans (regardless of focus) with a small set of standard competitive game formats.

Three structural observations matter for future Volleycraft plan-builder work:

1. **Defense grammar mirrors attack grammar but with different skills.** Plan 12's progression — per-shot technique → movement-between-positions → integrated chain → competitive game — mirrors Plans 8 and 7 respectively. The per-shot drill in Plan 12 (`Partner Toss Dig to Cut Shot`) is the dig-side analog of Plan 8 Drills 2/3. The movement drill (`4 Steps to Paradise`) is the defense-side analog of Plan 5's `Footwork for Setting`. This means the captured BAB plan grammar is **focus-agnostic at the structural level** — the same shape (warm-up → primer → technique → integration → competitive) carries across passing, setting, attacking, and defense. Volleycraft's session archetypes already encode a similar structure (`warmup` → `technique` / `movement_proxy` → `main_skill` → `pressure` → `wrap`), and Plan 12 is the cleanest BAB confirmation that this structure generalizes.
2. **Drill-repurposing across focus areas is now a captured BAB pattern.** Plan 12 Drill 4 (`Serve a Spot - Dig Set Hit`) is the same physical drill as Plan 2 Drill 4 (`Serve Spot, Dig Set Hit`); Plan 12 Drill 6 (`Mini Games to 7 (First Ball Focused Shot)`) is the same physical drill as Plan 5 Drill 8 (`Mini Games to 7 (Two Players Battle) (Option 1)`); Plan 12 Drill 5 extends the existing competitive-transition alias chain to three plans (Plan 7 / Plan 10 / Plan 12). Future Volleycraft work should be aware that **a single BAB drill can be cited in multiple practice contexts with different focus framing**, and the cross-reference table needs to support that. This converges with Thesis T1 in `docs/research/practice-plan-authoring-synthesis.md` (focus is purpose, not a tag): the same drill can serve different practice purposes, and BAB authors that explicitly by reusing the drill across plans rather than authoring a new drill per focus.
3. `**4 Steps to Paradise` is now authoring-ready when the defense chain activates.** The Plan 12 Drill 3 capture establishes:
  - "Paradise" = cross-court defense position (the position you want to be in as a defender, watching the diagonal hitter)
  - "4 steps" = the prescribed footwork to transition between digging positions (crossover → step → plant → plant)
  - Drill setup uses 3 players: one defender, two simulated attackers at each antenna
  - The drill is structurally analogous to setting footwork (Plan 5 Drill 2's off-foot/net-foot sequence) but for defense

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Same Tier 3+ stance for all Plan 12 novel work.** `defense` is not a shipped `SkillFocus` and there are no current defensive drills in `app/src/data/drills.ts`. Plans 12 novel content (Drills 2 and 3) sits entirely in the Tier 3+ backlog alongside the attack-chain work from Plans 7-11.
- **Three Plan 12 drills repeat earlier source families with different names (drill-name aliasing).** Plan 12 Drill 4 ≡ Plan 2 Drill 4; Plan 12 Drill 6 ≡ Plan 5 Drill 8; Plan 12 Drill 5 ≡ Plan 7 Drill 7 ≡ Plan 10 Drill 8. The cross-reference table now declares these aliases inline. The aliasing-pattern observation from Thesis T8 is now strongly source-evidenced across multiple plan boundaries.
- `**Partner Toss Dig to Cut Shot` is a per-shot defensive technique candidate.** Future defense-chain authoring should treat it as a sibling to a `Partner Toss Dig to High Line` variant (not yet captured but structurally implied by parallel with Plan 8's HL/CS pair). Author the per-shot pair as sibling variants under one family rather than a single configurable drill, consistent with Thesis T8.
- `**4 Steps to Paradise` is the canonical defensive movement drill in BAB.** It is the defense-side analog of `Footwork for Setting`, which already maps to `d40` in M001. When the defense chain activates, `4 Steps to Paradise` is the strongest source-form candidate for a "footwork" rung at the foundation of the chain.
- **Plan 12 confirms the BAB practice-plan template generalizes across focus areas.** The Coaches Guide template (`docs/research/bab-source-material.md` Source 3 Essay 2) describes a practice flow of warm-up → single-person drills → two-person drills → team drills → competitive team drills → cool-down. Plan 12 follows this template with defense-focused content, just as Plans 1, 5, and 7 follow it with passing, setting, and attack content. This reinforces Thesis T1 (focus is purpose, not a tag) and the broader observation that BAB practices are structurally similar regardless of named focus.

Implementation consequences:

- **Plan 12 begins the captured BAB defense plan grammar.** Future defense-chain authoring should consult Plan 12's structure (per-shot dig technique → defensive movement → integrated chain → competitive wrapper) alongside FIVB chapter 7 (`docs/research/fivb-source-material.md`, 17 defense drills 7.1–7.17) and the BAB defensive vocabulary from the glossary.
- `**4 Steps to Paradise` re-solicitation caveat closes.** The Plan 12 cross-reference row is updated from "Defense-chain candidate (Tier 3+); name-only" to "source-detail captured." Future Volleycraft work can cite Plan 12 Drill 3 as canonical source.
- `**Partner Toss Dig to Cut Shot` argues for a per-shot dig family.** Author it as a sibling per-shot variant alongside a future `Partner Toss Dig to High Line` (or whatever the high-line-dig drill is named when surfaced). Per Thesis T8, prefer one drill record per named shot rather than a configurable parent. Plan 12 captures only the cut-shot version; the high-line sibling is structurally implied but not source-confirmed yet.
- **The drill-repurposing-across-focus pattern is now captured BAB evidence.** Future Volleycraft session-builder logic should be aware that the same drill record can be selected for different `skillFocus` values when the practice problem changes — without authoring duplicate records per focus. This converges with Thesis T1 (focus is purpose, not a tag).
- **The cross-reference table now declares three more aliases inline.** With Plan 12's three new aliasing cases (Drills 4, 5, 6), the multi-name-aware table format is now load-bearing across at least seven separate aliasing observations spanning Plans 2 / 5 / 7 / 8 / 9 / 10 / 11 / 12. The table format should be formalized before the attack or defense chain ships.

### Practice Plan 13 — partial source capture (founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **second BAB defensive practice plan** captured at source-detail level. Drill 1 (Best Warm Up Ever) is the standard repeated source family with a parenthetical framing hint `(Dig from Knees)` calling out the warmup's defender-only knees-to-sprawl segment; Drills 2–9 are captured in full. Plan 13 supplies two genuinely new defense drills (`Dig from Knees` and `Hand Dig / Platform Dig Set`), extends six alias chains, and provides the strongest evidence yet for **drill-repurposing across focus** by reframing the per-shot HL/CS drills from the defender's perspective rather than the attacker's.

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever (Dig from Knees)** *(name only; standard repeated source family)*: Source text identical to the universal BAB opener captured in Plans 1–12. The Plan 13 parenthetical `(Dig from Knees)` is a framing hint that calls out the existing warmup item *"Defender only: starting from knees to lay-down sprawl dig — 8 each side"* rather than a new drill — but the parenthetical is also a forward pointer to Plan 13 Drill 2, which formalizes the dig-from-knees motion as a standalone drill.

**Drill 2 — Dig from Knees** (10 min): P1 starts on knees about 2 ft from the sideline and 10 ft off the net. Before beginning, P1 lays down and completes a **"sand angel"** to show their reach. P2 tosses the ball **lower than the bottom of the net**, forcing P1 to lay down and complete a **one-handed scoop dig** back to P2. The dig should get higher than the antenna and remain on the defender's side of the net. Complete on both sides of the court using both hands.

This is a **new emergency-extension defensive technique drill** — the first BAB source for an isolated low-ball scoop-dig drill. The "sand angel" reach assessment is also new vocabulary: the player lays flat in the sand and stretches arms and legs out to mark their physical reach radius, establishing where they can and cannot reach a ball from a knees-down starting position. The drill trains:

- Low-ball recognition (the toss is intentionally below net height)
- One-handed scoop technique (not platform/forearms)
- Controlled return trajectory (above antenna height, on own side of the net)
- Both-hand symmetry (cycle through both hands)

**Drill 3 — Toss to Dig Cut/HL Shot** (10 min): **Same source form as Plan 12 Drill 2 (`Partner Toss Dig to Cut Shot`)** with a different drill name. Source text matches verbatim — P1 at the starting position for digging a hard-angle attack; P2 at the net tossing a cut shot; P1 uses one crossover step plus laydown/dive to dig and lift to antenna height; switch left-side / right-side. The Plan 13 drill name implies an HL variant could fold in (`Cut/HL Shot`), but the captured source text only describes the cut-shot version. Treat this as a drill-name aliasing case where Plan 13 hints at a high-line dig sibling without supplying its source text.

**Drill 4 — Hand Dig / Platform Dig Set - 2 sets** (15 min): Players 1 and 2 are both on the south side of the court. P1 starts at the net on the east sideline; P2 is in the court ready to dig a cross-court attack from P1. The attack is at P2's head, **forcing P2 to use hands (overhand "hand dig") to defend**, not platform/forearms.

- P1 hits a ball at P2's head or higher
- P2 digs the hit **with hands** (hand dig)
- P1 sets the ball that P2 dug
- P2 sets the ball back to P1
- P2 **releases back to defense** and digs another ball from P1
- Repeat steps 1–5 for a certain amount of reps; switch jobs

This is a **new multi-touch defensive sequence drill**. It introduces three pieces of new BAB vocabulary at once: **hand dig** (using hands overhand to defend a hard ball at chest/head height, instead of platform/forearms), **platform dig** (the standard forearm dig, contrasted here with hand dig), and **release back to defense** (the transition motion after a contact where the defender returns to defensive position to receive the next attack). The drill chains the three skills with a midstream set return, training:

- Hand-dig technique against a high hard ball
- Set return as a defensive third contact
- Transition release back to defense for a second attack
- Drill stamina (5-step cycle repeats with role swap)

**Drill 5 — Toss to HL** (10 min): **Same source form as Plan 8 Drill 2 (`Hitting a High Line`) and Plan 9 Drill 4 (`Offensive Accuracy - HL`)** with a different drill name and **defender-perspective framing**. Source text matches the per-shot HL drill but the Plan 13 explanation explicitly ends with *"Player 1 reacts and catches shot"* — emphasizing the tosser-becomes-defender role rather than the attacker's HL technique. The drill is unchanged; the practice context has shifted from attack to defense.

**Drill 6 — Toss to Cut Shot** (10 min): **Same source form as Plan 8 Drill 3 (`Hitting a Cut Shot`) and Plan 9 Drill 5 (`Offensive Accuracy - CS`)** with a different drill name and defender-perspective framing. Same observation as Drill 5 — same drill, defensive framing. The drill is the cut-shot sibling to Drill 5.

**Drill 7 — HL - Cut Shot - to Open Net** (15 min): **Same source form as Plan 7 Drill 5 (`Highlines - Cuts - Open Net Swing`)** with a different drill name. Source text matches verbatim — 4 players, P1 tosses, P2 blocks, P3/P4 pass-set-attack designated shot, P1 digs and attacks on open net, defender always sits cross-court, switch from HL to CS after rotation. This is another drill-name aliasing case.

**Drill 8 — HL - Cut Shot - Live** (20 min): **Same source form as Plan 7 Drill 7 / Plan 10 Drill 8 / Plan 12 Drill 5** (the Comp Transition family). Plan 13 extends the existing alias chain to four plans for the same competitive transition drill. Plan 13 drill name (`HL - Cut Shot - Live`) is the shortest of the four names. Source text matches verbatim.

**Drill 9 — 14-15 Games to 21** (30 min): **Same source form as Plan 9 Drill 7 / Plan 10 Drill 9 / Plan 11 Drill 6** (the 14-15 Games competitive wrapper family). Plan 13 does not lock a specific best-of value (says "best of 3/5/7 depending on time"), unlike Plan 10 (best of 3) and Plan 11 (best of 5). Source text matches Plan 9's framing.

### Practice Plan 13 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 13 is the second defense-focused BAB plan and it deepens the captured BAB defense plan grammar with **two new defensive technique drills**, **defender-perspective framing of per-shot drills already captured in attack plans**, and **six aliasing extensions** that strengthen the multi-name-aware cross-reference table. Where Plan 12 established the defense plan structural grammar (warm-up → per-shot dig → defensive movement → integrated chain → competitive wrapper), Plan 13 fills in two more layers of the defensive technique foundation:

- **Plan 13 Drill 2 (`Dig from Knees`)** is an isolated emergency-extension drill that trains low-ball scoop dig from a near-ground starting position. It pairs with Plan 12 Drill 2 (`Partner Toss Dig to Cut Shot`, which trains lateral-extension dig with crossover + dive) to form a **two-drill defensive technique foundation pair**: low-ball-from-low and lateral-from-low. Both drills emphasize the same target (lift to antenna height) but train different reach problems.
- **Plan 13 Drill 4 (`Hand Dig / Platform Dig Set`)** is a multi-touch defensive sequence drill that trains hand-dig technique (overhand at chest/head height), set return as a third contact, and the transition release back to defense for a second attack. This drill is structurally distinct from Plans 12 and 13 Drill 2/3 because it emphasizes **continuous defensive engagement** rather than isolated dig technique.

Three structural observations matter for future Volleycraft plan-builder work:

1. **Plan 13 supplies the strongest evidence yet for Thesis T1 drill-repurposing across focus.** Plan 13 Drills 5 and 6 are the same per-shot HL/CS drills as Plans 8/9 (the canonical attack-focus per-shot technique drills), but Plan 13 frames them from the defender's perspective rather than the attacker's. The drill name shifts from `Hitting a HL` / `Offensive Accuracy - HL` to `Toss to HL`, and the explanation explicitly ends with *"Player 1 reacts and catches shot"* — the tosser-becomes-defender role becomes the named focus. **The drill is unchanged; the practice context frames the emphasis.** This is the cleanest BAB evidence captured so far that the same drill can serve attack-focus and defense-focus practices by reframing the named focus character. Future Volleycraft plan-builder work can cite Plan 13 Drills 5 and 6 alongside Plan 12 Drill 4 as the two strongest source cases for drill-repurposing-across-focus.
2. **Six aliasing extensions in one plan is a discipline signal.** Plan 13 extends or creates aliases for Plan 12 Drill 2, Plan 8 Drill 2 / Plan 9 Drill 4, Plan 8 Drill 3 / Plan 9 Drill 5, Plan 7 Drill 5, the Comp Transition family (now four plans), and the 14-15 Games wrapper family. With Plan 13, the cross-reference table is multi-name aware across at least eight separate aliasing observations spanning Plans 2 / 5 / 7 / 8 / 9 / 10 / 11 / 12 / 13. Every defensive plan captured so far reuses earlier source forms with different names — meaning **the alias mechanism is not optional for defense-chain authoring**; it is load-bearing.
3. **The defensive technique foundation is now a four-drill set.** Captured BAB defensive technique drills:
  - Plan 12 Drill 2 (`Partner Toss Dig to Cut Shot`) — lateral-extension cut-shot dig with crossover + dive
  - Plan 13 Drill 2 (`Dig from Knees`) — low-ball one-handed scoop dig with sand-angel reach assessment
  - Plan 13 Drill 3 (`Toss to Dig Cut/HL Shot`) — alias of Plan 12 Drill 2 with HL extension hint (HL source text not yet captured)
  - Plan 13 Drill 4 (`Hand Dig / Platform Dig Set`) — multi-touch hand-dig + set + release sequence
  - Plus the implied future siblings (high-line dig version of Plan 12 Drill 2, structural sibling per Thesis T8 per-shot variant pattern)
   Future defense-chain authoring should sequence these as foundation rungs: emergency low-ball dig → lateral cut-shot dig → high-line dig (when source captured) → multi-touch hand-dig sequence → defensive movement (`4 Steps to Paradise`) → integrated chain → competitive wrapper.

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Same Tier 3+ stance for all Plan 13 novel work.** `defense` is not a shipped `SkillFocus` and there are no current defensive drills in `app/src/data/drills.ts`. Plan 13's two new drills (Drills 2 and 4) sit entirely in the Tier 3+ backlog alongside Plan 12's defensive content.
- **Five Plan 13 drills are repeats of earlier source families with different names (drill-name aliasing) and one extends an existing alias chain.** The cross-reference table now declares all aliases inline. The aliasing-pattern observation from Thesis T8 is now strongly source-evidenced across multiple plan boundaries — every defensive plan captured so far reuses earlier source forms.
- **The "sand angel" reach-assessment ritual is a small but concrete BAB authoring pattern.** Before drilling, the player marks their physical reach radius by laying flat and stretching out. This is structurally similar to FIVB's "feel for conditions" warmup item (`docs/research/beach-training-resources.md`) — both are pre-drill rituals that calibrate the player to their actual physical envelope. Future Volleycraft drill copy could use a similar pre-drill calibration cue if courtside time permits, but it is content-polish territory, not a structural pattern.
- **Hand dig / platform dig is a beach-defense vocabulary distinction.** FIVB beach passing essay (`docs/research/fivb-source-material.md` Passing essay) calls out the **tomahawk** as a two-hand overhead emergency touch and the deeper-receiving-position rule that lets passers avoid overhead-only situations. Plan 13's `hand dig` is a different technique (overhand defense against a hard-driven ball at chest/head height) and a different scenario (defense reading a hard hit, not serve receive). When the defense chain activates, the catalog needs to distinguish `tomahawk` (passing emergency) from `hand dig` (defensive technique against a hard hit) cleanly.
- **Plan 13 Drill 2's "lower than the bottom of the net" toss is a calibration trick.** It guarantees the defender cannot reach the ball without going to ground, which forces the laydown/scoop motion every rep. Future Volleycraft drill authoring could borrow this calibration pattern (specify ball trajectory relative to a court reference) for any drill where a specific motion is the training target.
