Implementation consequences:

- **The defensive technique foundation is now a four-drill set across Plans 12–13.** Captured BAB drills: lateral-extension cut-shot dig (Plan 12 Drill 2), low-ball scoop dig (Plan 13 Drill 2), the cut-shot dig alias (Plan 13 Drill 3), and the multi-touch hand-dig sequence (Plan 13 Drill 4). The future high-line dig sibling is structurally implied (per Thesis T8) but not yet source-captured. Future defense-chain authoring should sequence these as foundation rungs.
- **Drill-repurposing across focus is no longer just a Plan 12 observation — it is a recurring BAB pattern.** Plan 12 reused `Serve a Spot - Dig Set Hit` and `Mini Games to 7` from earlier passing/setting plans; Plan 13 reuses the per-shot HL/CS drills from Plans 8/9 with explicit defender-perspective framing. **Volleycraft should not silently duplicate drills per focus area.** The session builder should select the same drill record for different `skillFocus` values when the practice problem aligns. Plan 13 is the cleanest source case for this pattern.
- **Plan 13 raises the importance of formalizing the alias mechanism.** With six aliasing extensions in a single plan, the multi-name-aware cross-reference table is now load-bearing across at least eight separate observations. The table format should be formalized before the attack or defense chain ships; ad-hoc inline declarations will not scale to a full BAB capture set.
- `**Hand dig` is distinct vocabulary from `tomahawk`.** FIVB's tomahawk (passing emergency, two-hand overhead, defensive against a serve at face) and Plan 13's hand dig (defensive against a hard hit at chest/head, overhand) are different techniques in different scenarios. Future catalog content should keep them separate; do not collapse them into a generic "overhand defensive contact" tag.
- **The "sand angel" pre-drill ritual is a calibration pattern worth borrowing.** Future Volleycraft drill authoring could surface a similar pre-drill calibration cue for any drill where physical reach or court geometry matters, but only as content-polish — it is not a structural pattern requiring schema support.

### Practice Plan 14 — partial source capture (founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **third BAB defensive practice plan** captured at source-detail level. Drill 1 (Best Warm Up Ever) is the standard repeated source family; Drills 2–7 are captured in full. Plan 14 supplies one new 4-player pull-block-dig drill (`Pull Digs to Set`), a sibling per-shot pair of smack-misdirection shuffle-dig drills (`Shuffle to High Line Dig` / `Shuffle to Cut Shot Dig`), and extends two existing alias chains (Comp Transition reaches five plans; the 14-15 Games wrapper extends similarly). Plan 14's smack-misdirection pattern is the **first BAB source for an attacker-deception read drill** — distinct from Plan 9's `3 Touch Vision Pepper` (which reads defender hand position) and Plan 11's `Beat the Blocker` (which reads blocker action) because here the *attacker* is the deceiver, faking one shot type with a smack and then actually delivering a different shot.

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** *(name only; standard repeated source family)*: Source text identical to the universal BAB opener captured in Plans 1–13.

**Drill 2 — Triangle Setting** (10–20 min): **Same source form as Plan 10 Drill 2 and Plan 11 Drill 2** — the 4-player hit-fed Triangle Setting with the level-scaled continuous-vs-catch rule. Source text identical across Plans 10, 11, and 14. Plan 14 confirms this as the most-repeated 4-player Triangle Setting source form in the captured set.

**Drill 3 — Pull Digs to Set** *(no time captured)*: P1 is at the net (attacker), facing P2 and P3 who alternate as blockers/diggers. P4 is the setter. Two scenarios:

- **Pull into the line:** Blocker pulls off the net into the line, digs an attack from P1, P4 sets the dig back to P1; P2 and P3 alternate as the digging blocker. Complete on both sides of the court; repeat for all players.
- **Pull into the angle:** Blocker pulls off the net into the angle, digs an attack from P1, **P4 sets the ball back to the blocker** (not back to P1), allowing the blocker to set the ball back to P1 as a third contact. Complete on both sides of the court; repeat for all players.

This is the first BAB source for `**pull dig` source-detail** beyond glossary level. The drill formalizes BAB's pull-dig vocabulary (blocker disengages from net to play defense) into two named scenarios — pull-line and pull-angle — and adds a transition-setting variant where the blocker becomes the setter for their own dig (scenario b). Note: the source text has a typo "angel" for "angle" — the canonical archive spelling is "angle." Plan 14 also introduces `**transition setting`** as named BAB vocabulary: a player setting after their own previous defensive contact (the blocker who just dug becomes the setter on the third contact).

**Drill 4 — Shuffle to High Line Dig** (10 min): P1 is at the net (attacker). P2 and P3 alternate digging high-line shots. P4 acts as a blocker working on **transition setting**. P1 **smacks the ball, then tosses** a retrievable shot (the smack signals "hit incoming"; the toss is the actual shot). On the smack, P2 and P3 start to **shuffle towards the angle**. **Right before contact, the diggers should change direction** to go dig the actual shot. P4 turns, chases, and sets the dig back to P1. Repeat so each player gets a chance to dig; complete on both sides of the court.

This is the first BAB source for an **attacker-deception read drill**. The smack is a deliberate misdirection: the attacker fakes a hard hit by smacking the ball, which tells the defender "hit incoming," so the defender starts shuffling towards the angle (where a hard hit would land). Then the attacker actually tosses a retrievable shot, and the defender must read the toss late and change direction to go dig the actual shot. The drill trains:

- Smack-recognition: hearing/seeing the smack and starting movement
- Late-read: detecting that the smack was a fake before final contact
- Change-of-direction: aborting the wrong-direction shuffle and pivoting to the actual shot
- Transition setting: P4 (blocker role) becomes the setter after the dig

**Drill 5 — Shuffle to Cut Shot Dig** (10 min): Same source form as Drill 4 but the actual shot is a cut shot instead of a high line. Sibling per-shot variant per Thesis T8.

**Drill 6 — Competitive - HL - CS - To Live Play** (30 min): **Same source form as Plan 7 Drill 7 / Plan 10 Drill 8 / Plan 12 Drill 5 / Plan 13 Drill 8** (the Comp Transition family). Plan 14 extends the existing alias chain to **five plans** for the same competitive transition drill. Plan 14's name matches Plan 10 Drill 8 capitalization exactly.

**Drill 7 — 14-15 Games to 21, Best of 5** (remainder of practice): **Same source form as Plan 11 Drill 6** with the same "Best of 5" parameter locking. Source text matches Plan 11 verbatim. The 14-15 Games wrapper is now captured across Plans 9, 10, 11, 13, and 14.

### Practice Plan 14 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 14 is the third defense-focused BAB plan and it deepens the captured BAB defense plan grammar with **two structurally novel drill patterns**:

1. `**Pull Digs to Set` (Drill 3)** is the first BAB source for a 4-player pull-block-and-transition-set drill. It formalizes pull-dig vocabulary into two named scenarios (line vs angle) and adds a transition-setting variant where the digger becomes the setter on the third contact. Distinct from Plan 12's `4 Steps to Paradise` (which is movement between dig positions, not pull-block-dig) and Plan 13's `Hand Dig / Platform Dig Set` (which is hand-dig at chest/head, not blocker pull-dig). The pull-dig family is structurally closer to FIVB chapter 7 defensive content than to the cross-court-defense drills earlier in the captured BAB defense set.
2. `**Shuffle to HL / CS Dig` (Drills 4–5)** is the first BAB source for an **attacker-deception read drill** — the attacker smacks the ball to fake a hard hit, then actually tosses a finesse shot, forcing the defender to change direction late. This is structurally distinct from prior read drills:
  - Plan 9 Drill 3 (`3 Touch Vision Pepper`): reads **defender hand position** (defender is the deceiver-by-choice)
  - Plan 11 Drill 5 (`Beat the Blocker`): reads **blocker action** (blocker is the deceiver-by-choice)
  - Plan 14 Drills 4–5 (`Shuffle to HL/CS Dig`): reads **attacker deception** (attacker is the deceiver via the smack-then-toss misdirection)
   These three plans together form a small captured taxonomy of read drills where the deceiver role rotates through different positions.

Three structural observations matter for future Volleycraft plan-builder work:

1. **The smack-then-toss misdirection is a calibration pattern, not a real attack.** The attacker doesn't actually hit hard — the smack is a deliberate vocal/visual cue to start the defender on the wrong path, then the toss delivers the real shot. This is a coaching-tool pattern (similar to Plan 13 Drill 2's "lower than the bottom of the net" toss calibration) where the drill controls the timing of the defender's read by manipulating the feed. Future Volleycraft drill authoring should model this as a **feed pattern** rather than a feed-type primitive — the toss is partner-fed, but the *misdirection* is the training target.
2. **Transition setting is now named BAB vocabulary.** Plans 5/6 used "set back to passer" framing (the setter sets to the named target); Plan 14 names the pattern explicitly: a player who just contributed a previous defensive contact (dig or block) becomes the setter on the third contact. This is structurally important for future defense-chain authoring because it implies the player role is dynamic within a rally, not fixed by position.
3. **Plan 14 confirms the alias-mechanism load.** Two more chain extensions in one plan (Comp Transition to five plans; 14-15 Games to four plans counting Plan 14, plus Plan 13's earlier extension) plus the Triangle Setting (4p hit-fed) confirmation across Plans 10/11/14. Every defense plan captured so far carries multiple aliases, and the rate is accelerating (Plan 13 added six aliases; Plan 14 adds two more chain extensions plus a Triangle Setting confirmation). The **alias mechanism must be in place before any defense-chain catalog ships** or the catalog will quietly grow duplicate-near-duplicate records.

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Same Tier 3+ stance for all Plan 14 novel work.** `defense` is not a shipped `SkillFocus` and there are no current defensive drills in `app/src/data/drills.ts`. Plan 14's three new drills (3, 4, 5) sit entirely in the Tier 3+ backlog alongside Plans 12-13's defensive content.
- **Four Plan 14 drills are repeats of earlier source families.** Drill 1 (universal opener), Drill 2 (Triangle Setting 4p hit-fed, repeated from Plans 10/11), Drill 6 (Comp Transition, extending the alias chain to five plans), Drill 7 (14-15 Games wrapper, extending the alias chain).
- **The defensive technique foundation is now a six-drill set across Plans 12–14.** Plan 12 Drill 2 (lateral cut-shot dig), Plan 12 Drill 3 (`4 Steps to Paradise` movement), Plan 13 Drill 2 (low-ball scoop), Plan 13 Drill 4 (multi-touch hand-dig sequence), Plan 14 Drill 3 (pull-block-dig with transition set), Plan 14 Drills 4–5 (smack-misdirection HL/CS shuffle-dig). These cover six distinct defensive scenarios. Plus aliases via Plan 13 Drills 5 and 6 (defender-perspective HL/CS technique).
- **The smack-misdirection pattern strengthens Thesis T10 (read/look-and-react drills).** T10 names read drills as a distinct subkind. Plan 14 extends T10 with a third deceiver position: not just defender (Plan 9) or blocker (Plan 11), but **attacker** (Plan 14). Future Volleycraft attack/defense content should treat the deceiver role as a per-drill axis (`deceiver: 'defender' | 'blocker' | 'attacker' | 'none'`) rather than a fixed property of the drill family.
- `**Pull Digs to Set` connects to FIVB chapter 7 defense.** FIVB has 17 defense drills (7.1–7.17, see `docs/research/fivb-source-material.md`). Plan 14 Drill 3 is the strongest BAB analog to FIVB's pull-block-and-defense work. Future defense-chain authoring should consult both sources together when scoping the pull-dig family.

Strongest BAB source for the attacker-deception subkind of read drills (sibling to Plan 9 Drill 3 defender-deception and Plan 11 Drill 5 blocker-deception).                                                                                                                                                        | `participants.min: 4`; `feedType: partner-toss` (the smack is a fake; the toss is the real feed); `needsNet: true`; `skillFocus: ['defense']` with `movement` as supporting. The smack-then-toss misdirection should be modeled as a **feed pattern** (drill metadata describing the cue/feed sequence) rather than a feed-type primitive. `successMetric.type: reps-successful` against "diggers changed direction in time + dug the actual shot." Cap total reps; the change-of-direction motion is high-impact on knees and ankles. Pair with `Shuffle to Cut Shot Dig` as sibling per-shot variants. |
| **Shuffle to Cut Shot Dig**              | Same source form as Drill 4 but the actual shot is a cut shot instead of a high line. Sibling per-shot variant.                                                                                                                                                                                                    | Tier 3+ defense-chain candidate; sibling per-shot variant of Drill 4.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Same authoring notes as Drill 4. Author the per-shot pair as sibling variants under one family rather than two separate records, per Thesis T8. The smack is the same; only the actual shot differs.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| **Competitive - HL - CS - To Live Play** | Same source form as Plan 7 Drill 7 / Plan 10 Drill 8 / Plan 12 Drill 5 / Plan 13 Drill 8 (the Comp Transition family). Plan 14 extends the existing alias chain to **five plans**.                                                                                                                                 | Tier 3+ modified-game candidate; one drill family with five BAB names now (Plans 7 / 10 / 12 / 13 / 14).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Treat as one record with five BAB names. Cross-reference table extended. Plan 14 name matches Plan 10's capitalization exactly.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| **14-15 Games to 21, Best of 5**         | Same source form as Plan 11 Drill 6 with the same "Best of 5" parameter. Plan 14 extends the existing alias chain.                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Tier 3+ session-wrapper candidate; one wrapper with five BAB names now (Plans 9 / 10 / 11 / 13 / 14). Should not become a standalone catalog drill record.                                                                                                                                                                                           | Treat as one wrapper with multiple BAB names and parameter values.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |


Implementation consequences:

- `**Pull Digs to Set` is authoring-ready when the defense chain activates.** The Plan 14 capture establishes the pull-dig vocabulary (line vs angle scenarios), the transition-setting variant, and the 4-player source form. Future defense-chain authoring can cite Plan 14 Drill 3 as canonical source and cross-reference FIVB chapter 7 for parallel defensive content.
- **The smack-misdirection feed pattern needs schema support.** Plan 14 Drills 4–5 train defenders to read late by deliberately faking the feed. A feed-type primitive (`partner-toss`, `live-serve`, etc.) cannot express this — the misdirection is a temporal feed pattern, not a feed type. Future Volleycraft drill metadata may need a `feedPattern` field separate from `feedType` to express patterns like smack-then-toss, scrambled-free-ball, or set-then-attack.
- **The deceiver-position axis is a candidate for read-drill schema support.** Plans 9 (defender-deception), 11 (blocker-deception), and 14 (attacker-deception) form a three-cell taxonomy. Future read drills could expose a `deceiverRole` axis (`'defender' | 'blocker' | 'attacker' | 'none'`) so the catalog can express which player is the deceiver in each drill.
- **Transition setting is a named BAB pattern that should not be silently merged into "set" skillFocus.** A player who sets after their own previous defensive contact (dig or block) is in a different role than a fixed setter. Future Volleycraft catalog should distinguish dedicated-setter drills from transition-setter drills, even if both fall under `skillFocus: 'set'`.
- **Three more aliases extend the chain reach.** Plan 14 confirms Triangle Setting (4p hit-fed) across Plans 10/11/14, extends Comp Transition to five plans, and extends the 14-15 Games wrapper. The cross-reference table format is now load-bearing across at least nine separate aliasing observations.

### Practice Plan 15 — partial source capture (founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **fourth BAB defensive practice plan** captured at source-detail level. Drills 1 (Best Warm Up Ever) and 2 (Triangle Setting) are name-only — the Triangle Setting source form is structurally implied to be the 4-player hit-fed variant from Plans 10/11/14 but not source-confirmed in Plan 15. Drills 3–8 are captured in full. Plan 15 supplies one new integrated drill (`Shuffle to High Line/Cut Shot to Live Play`, the competitive-integration of the Plan 14 Shuffle pair), one new rule-restriction variant (`Mini Games to 7 (SHOTS ONLY)` with a "win by 2" scoring rule), and confirms `4 Steps to Paradise` source-detail across two plans (12 and 15).

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** *(name only; standard repeated source family)*: Source text identical to the universal BAB opener captured in Plans 1–14.

**Drill 2 — Triangle Setting** *(name only; structurally implied 4-player hit-fed variant)*: No source text provided in the Plan 15 founder capture. The Triangle Setting drill name is shared across multiple BAB plans with at least four distinct source forms; Plan 15's drill is structurally implied to be the same 4-player hit-fed source form captured in Plans 10, 11, and 14 (the most-repeated Triangle Setting source form across the captured set), but Plan 15 does not confirm this. Re-solicit the source text if the source form matters for future authoring.

**Drill 3 — 4 Steps to Paradise** (10–20 min): **Same source form as Plan 12 Drill 3** with identical source text. Players 1, 2, and 3 are all on the south side of the net. P1 is on the court facing the net. P2 and P3 are at each antenna facing the endline's diagonal corner. P1 works on digging the ball in the cross-court defense position looking at the diagonal hitter, then completes a 4-step process (crossover, step, plant, plant) to get to the next digging spot. Plan 15 confirms the `4 Steps to Paradise` drill is a stable BAB source family; its earlier name-only TOC mention from Plan 15 (referenced in the Plan 12 cross-reference row) is now upgraded to source-detail confirmed.

**Drill 4 — Shuffle to High Line Dig** (10 min): **Same source form as Plan 14 Drill 4** with identical source text. Plan 15 extends the existing Shuffle to HL Dig drill to two plans. Source text matches verbatim including the smack-misdirection feed pattern.

**Drill 5 — Shuffle to Cut Shot Dig** (10 min): **Same source form as Plan 14 Drill 5** with identical source text. Plan 15 extends the existing Shuffle to CS Dig drill to two plans.

**Drill 6 — Shuffle to High Line/Cut Shot to Live Play** (20 min): Team A is on the south side of the court practicing picking up a cut shot (Round 1) and a high line (Round 2) while Team B is tossing the shots from the north side. **It should have a similar feel to the previous drill** (the Shuffle to HL/CS Dig drills) **with the shuffle to pick up the shot. Once the shot is picked up, finish the point as a live point.** Allow each team to dig and transition 10 balls and then switch jobs.

This is the **competitive-integration version of the Plan 14 Shuffle drills**. Plans 14 Drills 4-5 trained the controlled smack-then-toss misdirection in isolated technique form; Plan 15 Drill 6 takes the same shuffle-and-dig pattern and chains it into a live point. Structurally parallel to how Plan 7 Drill 7 / Plan 14 Drill 6 (`Comp Transition HL - CS - Live`) is the live-play extension of earlier per-shot work — the BAB plan grammar consistently couples a controlled-feed drill with a live-point integration drill that uses the same target shot.

The "(Round 1)" and "(Round 2)" notation in Plan 15 Drill 6 echoes the Round-N convention from the Mini Games to 7 family (Plan 5 Drill 8, Plan 8 Drill 8, Plan 12 Drill 6) but here the rounds are session-shape parameters rather than first-ball shot constraints — Plan 15 Drill 6's rounds determine which shot the diggers practice in each round, not which shot must happen on the first ball of a normal game.

**Drill 7 — Mini Games to 7 (SHOTS ONLY)** (20 min): A normal game to 7, **win by 2**, but the team can only score by shooting the ball. **No hard-driven attacks.** The work for this drill is picking up shots as a defender and using vision to score.

This is a **fourth documented rule-restriction variant of the Mini Games to 7 family**. The captured set now has:

- **Plan 5 Drill 8 / Plan 12 Drill 6** (`Two Players Battle (Option 1)` / `First Ball Focused Shot`): first-ball shot constraint on each round (Round 1 Cut Shot, Round 2 High Line, etc.)
- **Plan 8 Drill 8** (`Round 1 and 2 ONLY`): subset of the parent's round set (only Cut Shot and High Line rounds)
- **Plan 15 Drill 7** (`SHOTS ONLY`): every attack must be a shot, no hard-driven hits, with a "win by 2" scoring extension

This is the strongest source evidence yet that the Mini Games to 7 family should be modeled as a **single base drill with rule-restriction parameters** rather than as multiple separate records. The four documented variants share the same base game-to-7 structure and differ only in the constraint overlay. The "win by 2" scoring rule is also new vocabulary — a standard volleyball game-extension rule, but Plan 15 is the first BAB capture that names it explicitly.

**Drill 8 — 14-15 Games to 21, Best of 3** (remainder of practice): **Same source form as Plan 10 Drill 9** with the "Best of 3" parameter. Plan 15 extends the 14-15 Games wrapper alias chain to **six plans** (Plans 9 / 10 / 11 / 13 / 14 / 15).

### Practice Plan 15 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 15 is the fourth defense-focused BAB plan and it is structurally a **repetition + extension** plan rather than a novel-content plan. Six of its eight drills are repeats of earlier source families (Drills 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 8), and the two genuinely new contributions (Drills 6 and 7) are both **integration / variant** patterns rather than wholly new drill families:

- **Drill 6** (`Shuffle to High Line/Cut Shot to Live Play`) is the live-point integration of Plan 14 Drills 4–5, parallel to how Plan 7 Drill 7 / Plan 14 Drill 6 (`Comp Transition HL - CS - Live`) is the live-point integration of earlier per-shot work. This confirms a recurring BAB plan-grammar pattern: **controlled-feed technique drill → live-point integration drill** with the same target shot.
- **Drill 7** (`Mini Games to 7 (SHOTS ONLY)`) is a fourth documented rule-restriction variant of the Mini Games to 7 family. Plus a new "win by 2" scoring rule.

Three structural observations matter for future Volleycraft plan-builder work:

1. **The Mini Games to 7 family now has at least four documented rule-restriction variants.** Plan 5 / Plan 12 (First Ball Focused Shot / Two Players Battle), Plan 8 (Round 1 and 2 ONLY), Plan 15 (SHOTS ONLY). This sharpens Thesis T9 (rule-restricted/augmented variants): Volleycraft modeling that supports only one variant per record will fragment the Mini Games to 7 family into four near-duplicate records, each consuming a row of the authoring-budget cap. The single-base-drill-with-parameters approach is much stronger for this family. Plan 15 is the strongest case yet for **runtime constraint toggles** (T9 Option 3) over separate records (Option 1).
2. **The "controlled-feed → live-point integration" pattern is now a recurring BAB plan grammar.** Captured pairs:
  - Plans 8/9 per-shot HL/CS technique → Plan 7 Drill 7 (Comp Transition Live)
  - Plan 14 Shuffle to HL/CS Dig → Plan 15 Drill 6 (Shuffle to HL/CS to Live Play)
  - (FIVB modified games are the broader source for this pattern; BAB shows multiple instances)
   This is structurally the same as the rule-delta-game pattern but applied at a different layer: instead of constraining a normal game with a rule delta (BAB Mini Games to 7 family), this pattern takes a controlled drill and removes the controlled-feed constraint so it plays out live. Future Volleycraft session-builder logic could expose this as a session-level pairing rule: when a controlled-feed drill has a known live-point sibling, sequence them in the same session for transfer.
3. `**4 Steps to Paradise` is now confirmed as a stable BAB source form across two plans.** Plan 15's source text is identical to Plan 12. The cross-reference row's earlier "Plan 15 TOC also lists this drill" caveat upgrades to "source-detail confirmed across both plans." This reinforces Plan 12's `4 Steps to Paradise` as the canonical defensive movement drill for any future defense chain.

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Same Tier 3+ stance for all Plan 15 novel work.** `defense` is not a shipped `SkillFocus` and there are no current defensive drills in `app/src/data/drills.ts`. Plan 15's two new contributions (Drills 6 and 7) sit entirely in the Tier 3+ backlog alongside Plans 12-14's defensive content.
- **Six Plan 15 drills are repeats of earlier source families.** Drill 1 (universal opener), Drill 2 (Triangle Setting, name-only), Drill 3 (4 Steps to Paradise, source-confirming Plan 12), Drill 4 (Shuffle to HL, repeat of Plan 14), Drill 5 (Shuffle to CS, repeat of Plan 14), Drill 8 (14-15 Games wrapper, extending the alias chain to six plans).
- **Plan 15 reduces the urgency of formalizing the alias mechanism but does not eliminate it.** The alias-chain extensions in Plan 15 are pure repetition (no new drill names being added to existing chains) — Plan 15 confirms existing patterns rather than inventing new ones. But every aliasing observation from earlier plans still stands, and the cross-reference table is now multi-name aware across at least ten separate observations spanning Plans 2 / 5 / 7 / 8 / 9 / 10 / 11 / 12 / 13 / 14 / 15.
- **The `vision` cue from Plan 15 Drill 7 ("using vision to score") connects to Plan 9 Drill 3 (`3 Touch Vision Pepper`).** BAB uses "vision" as both a drill family marker (Plan 9 specifically) and a coaching concept (Plan 15 Drill 7's "use vision to score"). Future Volleycraft drill copy should treat "vision" as a defender-read concept that applies across multiple drill subkinds, not just one drill.
- **The "win by 2" scoring rule is BAB's first explicit named scoring extension.** Other BAB scoring formats (3 Before 5, +3/-3, Mini Games to 7, Set to 21) all have a clear win condition baked in. Plan 15 Drill 7 is the first capture where BAB names "win by 2" as an extension rule. Future Volleycraft authoring should treat scoring rules as composable: base (game to N points) + extension (win by margin / win by lead / etc.).

Use this table when deciding whether to add or adapt the Plan 15 drills to `app/src/data/drills.ts`.

Implementation consequences:

- **Plan 15 strengthens the case for the Mini Games to 7 family being a single base drill with parameter overlays.** With four documented rule-restriction variants now (First Ball Focused Shot, Round 1 and 2 ONLY, SHOTS ONLY, plus the original "play to 7 with first-ball shot constraints" base), the family cannot be cleanly split across four separate records without near-duplicate authoring. Future Volleycraft modeling should pick this as an early test case for T9 runtime-constraint-toggle modeling.
- `**Shuffle to HL/CS to Live Play` is authoring-ready when the defense chain activates.** The Plan 15 Drill 6 capture establishes the live-point integration pattern for the Shuffle drills. Future defense-chain authoring should pair the controlled-feed drills (Plan 14 Drills 4-5) with the live-play integration drill (Plan 15 Drill 6) in session-builder sequencing logic.
- **The "controlled-feed → live-point integration" pattern is a session-builder hint.** Captured BAB pairs: per-shot HL/CS (Plans 8/9) → Comp Transition Live (Plan 7 Drill 7); Shuffle to HL/CS Dig (Plan 14) → Shuffle to HL/CS to Live Play (Plan 15). Future session-builder logic could expose this as a sequencing rule that groups paired drills in adjacent slots when both are catalog-active.
- `**win by 2` is a composable scoring extension.** Plan 15 Drill 7 is the first BAB capture that names "win by 2" explicitly as an extension to a base scoring format. Future Volleycraft scoring metadata should support composable scoring rules (base + extension) rather than enumerating each combination as a separate scoring type.
- **Plan 15 confirms the `4 Steps to Paradise` and Shuffle drill source forms are stable across plans.** Cross-reference row updates should upgrade "Plan 15 TOC also lists" caveats to "source-detail confirmed across two plans."

### Practice Plan 16 — partial source capture (founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. This is the **fifth and final defensive practice plan** captured at source-detail level, **completing the captured Defensive cluster (Plans 12–16)**. Drills 1 (Best Warm Up Ever) and 2 (Triangle Setting) are name-only — Triangle Setting is structurally implied to be the 4-player hit-fed source form from Plans 10/11/14 but not source-confirmed. Drills 3–7 are captured in full. Plan 16 supplies a **structurally novel pair of read drills** (`Threat or No Threat` Drills 5 and 6 — the first BAB source for **blocker-as-reader drills** where the blocker reads set quality and decides between blocking and pulling off net to dig) plus a new competitive wrapper format (`Best of 3, Match to 21` with a `third-to-15` tiebreaker rule).

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** *(name only; standard repeated source family)*: Source text identical to the universal BAB opener captured in Plans 1–15.

**Drill 2 — Triangle Setting** *(name only; structurally implied 4-player hit-fed variant)*: No source text provided in the Plan 16 founder capture. Same status as Plan 15 Drill 2 — structurally implied to be the same 4-player hit-fed source form captured in Plans 10/11/14, but not source-confirmed. Plan 16 extends the Triangle Setting (4p hit-fed) name-only chain to two plans (15 and 16).

**Drill 3 — Pull Digs to Set** *(no time captured)*: **Same source form as Plan 14 Drill 3** with identical source text (including the "angel" typo for "angle"). P1 at the net (attacker), P2 and P3 alternate as blockers/diggers, P4 is the setter. Two scenarios: pull-into-line (P4 sets the dig back to P1; P2/P3 alternate) and pull-into-angle (P4 sets back to the blocker, who sets back to P1). Plan 16 confirms `Pull Digs to Set` as a stable BAB source family across two plans (14 and 16).

**Drill 4 — Cross Court Pepper** (10 min): **Same source form as Plan 5 Drill 6 / Plan 7 Drill 3 / Plan 11 Drill 3** — the 4-player cross-court pepper drill. Source text identical across all four plans. Plan 16 extends the existing alias chain to **four plans** (5, 7, 11, 16). Players 1 and 2 north (NW, NE), Players 3 and 4 south (SE, SW). Round 1: Players 2 and 4 dig and attack while Players 1 and 3 are "blocking" and setting. Each side gets three touches: pass, set, controlled attack. Continue for a rep count or back-and-forth goal, then switch roles.

**Drill 5 — Threat or No Threat** (20 min): Team A north, Team B south. A player from Team B starts the drill by tossing a ball to Team A. The other player from Team B is at the net acting as the blocker. Once the ball is tossed, Team A passes, sets, and hits the ball back to Team B.

- **If the set is good = the hitter is a THREAT, and the blocker should stay to block.**
- **If the set is bad or off the net = the hitter is NOT a THREAT, and the blocker should pull off the net to dig.**

The attacker can hit anywhere they want during this rally. Play out the point live after the toss. Each team gets 10 tosses (5 per person), then switch jobs.

This is a **blocker-as-reader drill** — the BLOCKER is the read-and-decide actor. The blocker reads the **quality of the set** (a teammate's contact, not an opponent's action) and decides between two committed actions (block vs pull off to dig). This is structurally distinct from prior captured read drills:

- Plan 9 Drill 3 (`3 Touch Vision Pepper`): defender hands signal → **attacker reads** opponent's defender
- Plan 11 Drill 5 (`Beat the Blocker`): blocker chooses → **attacker reads** opponent's blocker
- Plan 14 Drills 4–5 (`Shuffle to HL/CS Dig`): attacker smacks (deceiver) → **defender reads** opponent's attacker
- **Plan 16 Drills 5–6 (`Threat or No Threat`): set quality (teammate's contact) → blocker reads team-context cue and decides commit/pull**

Plan 16's read drill is the first BAB capture where the read is based on a **team-context cue (set quality)** rather than an opponent action. The reader is the blocker; the cue source is a teammate; the decision is between two committed defensive actions. This expands the read-drill taxonomy with a new axis: **reader role** (defender / blocker / attacker / blocker-pulled) is distinct from **deceiver role** (the prior taxonomy axis from Plans 9/11/14).

**Drill 6 — Threat or No Threat with Serve** (20 min): **Same source form as Drill 5 with serve-fed feed** instead of toss-fed. Identical structure: Team B player serves to Team A; Team A passes-sets-hits; the blocker reads set quality and decides block-vs-pull; play out live. Each team gets 10 tosses (sic — source text says "tosses" even though the feed is now a serve), 5 per person.

Drills 5 and 6 form a **toss-fed → serve-fed sibling pair** — same drill structure with the only difference being the feed type. This is structurally the same pattern as Plan 3's `Passing Triangle from Toss` → `Passing Triangle from Serve` pair. The BAB plan-grammar pattern of pairing a controlled-feed (toss) variant with a live-feed (serve) variant of the same drill is now confirmed across at least two plan family captures (Plan 3 passing, Plan 16 defense).

**Drill 7 — Best of 3, Match to 21** (remainder of practice): A normal volleyball match playing to 21. If it goes to a third match, play the third to 15.

This is a **new competitive wrapper format** distinct from prior captured wrappers:

- `14-15 Games to 21` (Plans 9, 10, 11, 13, 14, 15): compressed game starting at 14-15 instead of 0
- `Set to 21` (Plan 9): single set with side switches at 7s
- `Mini Games to 7` family (Plans 5, 8, 12, 15): multi-round modified games with first-ball shot constraints
- **Plan 16 Drill 7 `Best of 3, Match to 21`**: full match format with best-of-3 series and a `third-to-15` tiebreaker rule

The `third-to-15` tiebreaker is composable with the `win by 2` extension from Plan 15 — together they argue for **fully composable game-scoring metadata** (base score-to-N + tiebreaker-to-M + win-by-margin extension as independent parameters).

### Practice Plan 16 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 16 is the fifth and final defensive plan and **completes the captured Defensive cluster (Plans 12–16)**. The plan is structurally a **mix of repetition and one structurally novel contribution**: five of its seven drills are repeats of earlier source families (Drills 1, 2, 3, 4, 7's earlier-wrapper kin), and the two genuinely new drills (Drills 5 and 6) are a sibling pair introducing a new read-drill subkind that the captured set didn't previously contain.

Three structural observations matter for future Volleycraft plan-builder work:

1. **The captured BAB read-drill taxonomy now has four positions, not three.** Plan 14's introduction of attacker-deception read drills established a three-cell taxonomy (defender / blocker / attacker as deceiver). Plan 16 introduces a fourth position: **blocker-as-reader** with a **team-context cue** (set quality) rather than an opponent-action cue. This is structurally distinct enough to warrant treating "reader role" and "deceiver role" as **two separate axes** rather than one, with a third "cue source" axis (opponent action vs team-context):
  - Plan 9: reader=attacker, cue source=opponent (defender hands)
  - Plan 11: reader=attacker, cue source=opponent (blocker action)
  - Plan 14: reader=defender, cue source=opponent (attacker smack)
  - Plan 16: reader=blocker, cue source=team-context (teammate's set quality)
   Future Volleycraft attack/defense content authoring should be aware of this three-axis taxonomy: any read drill needs to specify reader role, cue source role, and cue type.
2. **The toss-fed → serve-fed sibling pair pattern is now confirmed across multiple captures.** Plan 3 Drills 4–5 (`Passing Triangle from Toss/Serve`) was the first BAB capture of this pattern; Plan 16 Drills 5–6 (`Threat or No Threat` toss-fed and serve-fed siblings) confirm it as a recurring BAB authoring pattern. Different from the controlled-feed → live-point integration pattern (Plan 7/14 Comp Transition; Plan 15 Shuffle to Live Play) because here both versions are full sideout chains with the same drill structure — the only difference is feed type. Future Volleycraft drill metadata should support pairing toss-fed and serve-fed siblings as variants on a single parent drill, similar to how per-shot HL/CS pairs are siblings per Thesis T8.
3. **The `Best of 3, Match to 21` wrapper with `third-to-15` tiebreaker confirms the composable scoring rules thesis.** Combined with Plan 15's `win by 2` extension, the captured set now has multiple composable scoring rule fragments: base game-to-N (where N varies by family — 7 for Mini Games to 7, 21 for 14-15 Games / Set to 21 / Match to 21), tiebreaker-to-M (Plan 16's `third-to-15`), and win-by-margin (Plan 15's `win by 2`). Future Volleycraft scoring metadata should treat these as **three independent parameters** rather than enumerating each combination as a separate scoring type.

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Same Tier 3+ stance for all Plan 16 novel work.** `defense` is not a shipped `SkillFocus` and there are no current defensive drills in `app/src/data/drills.ts`. Plan 16's two new drills (Drills 5 and 6) plus the new wrapper format (Drill 7) sit entirely in the Tier 3+ backlog alongside Plans 12-15's defensive content.
- **Five Plan 16 drills are repeats of earlier source families.** Drill 1 (universal opener), Drill 2 (Triangle Setting, name-only), Drill 3 (Pull Digs to Set, repeat of Plan 14), Drill 4 (Cross Court Pepper, extending the alias chain to four plans — Plans 5, 7, 11, 16). Drill 7's "Match to 21" format is structurally a new wrapper but composable with earlier wrapper rules.
- **Plan 16 completes the captured Defensive cluster with the cleanest decision-drill of the set.** `Threat or No Threat` is a binary-decision drill where the blocker has only two committed options (block vs pull) based on a clear cue (set quality good vs bad). This is structurally similar to Plan 11 Drill 5's `Beat the Blocker` (blocker chooses among grab/line/cross) but the *direction of decision flow* is reversed — in Plan 11 the blocker's choice is the cue for the attacker's read; in Plan 16 a teammate's set quality is the cue for the blocker's own read. Both are read-and-decide drills, but Plan 16 is the first where the blocker is the reader.
- **The blocker-pull mechanic ties Plan 16 back to Plan 14's `Pull Digs to Set`.** Plan 14 trains the pull-block-and-dig motion as isolated technique; Plan 16 trains the **decision** to pull (vs block) based on set quality. Future defense-chain authoring should sequence these as foundation → decision rungs: Plan 14's pull technique → Plan 16's threat-decision — pull is the option Plan 16 trains the blocker to choose.
- **The "match to 21" format connects to FIVB and traditional volleyball scoring.** Beach volleyball traditionally uses 21-point sets with rally scoring and a 15-point third set. Plan 16 Drill 7 matches this convention. Future Volleycraft session-builder logic could expose `match`, `set`, and `compressed-game` as three different wrapper categories with different default scoring rules.

Use this table when deciding whether to add or adapt the Plan 16 drills to `app/src/data/drills.ts`.

Implementation consequences:

- **Plan 16 completes the captured Defensive cluster (Plans 12–16).** Future defense-chain authoring now has a complete BAB defense plan grammar template: opener → Triangle Setting (setting touch) → defensive technique foundation (Plans 12-13) → defensive movement (Plan 12 `4 Steps to Paradise`) → smack-misdirection / pull-block / blocker-decision drills (Plans 14, 16) → controlled-feed → live-point integration (Plan 15) → competitive wrapper. This is the most complete single-focus plan grammar captured in the BAB set so far.
- **The blocker-as-reader axis is a new schema requirement.** Plan 16 Drills 5–6 cannot be modeled with the existing `deceiverRole` axis from Thesis T11; they need a separate `readerRole` axis. Future Volleycraft attack/defense content authoring should plan for **two independent role axes** on read drills: `readerRole` (who is reading) and `deceiverRole` or `cueSource` (where the cue comes from).
- **The toss-fed → serve-fed sibling pair pattern is now a recurring BAB authoring pattern.** Plan 3 (passing) and Plan 16 (defense) both use this pattern. Future Volleycraft drill metadata should support pairing toss-fed and serve-fed siblings as variants on a single parent drill, distinct from the controlled-feed → live-point integration pattern (where the second variant adds live-point play, not just a feed change).
- **Composable scoring rules are now a strong source-evidenced thesis.** Plan 15's `win by 2` + Plan 16's `third-to-15` tiebreaker confirm that BAB game-wrapper scoring is built from independent rule fragments. Future Volleycraft scoring metadata should support: base scoring (game-to-N format), tiebreaker (third-to-M for best-of series), and win-by-margin extension as three independent parameters.
- **Plan 16's `Threat or No Threat` ties together Plan 14's pull-block technique and a binary decision drill.** Pair them in session-builder sequencing logic: Plan 14's pull technique → Plan 16's threat-decision. The pull is the option Plan 16 trains the blocker to choose; without the technique foundation, the decision is harder to execute.

### Practice Plan 17 — partial source capture (founder capture)

Captured on 2026-05-04. The founder labeled this plan "defensive" in the paste, but the drill content is unambiguously **Game Play / pressure-game**: Race to 5 HL and CS (competitive accuracy race), 10 Sideouts (per-player sideout measurement format), 3 Before 5 (with a new BIG point elevation mechanic), and Games to 21 (full match). The labeling discrepancy is consistent with BAB's drill-book ordering, where Plans 17–20 form the **Game Play cluster** following the Defense cluster (Plans 12–16). Plan 17 is the **first Game Play plan captured at source-detail level**, and the first cluster representative for what the adversarial review on `docs/research/practice-plan-authoring-synthesis.md` named as the cluster best positioned to test whether the captured BAB plan grammar is genuinely focus-agnostic.

Drills 1 (Best Warm Up Ever) and 2 (Triangle Setting) are name-only — Triangle Setting is structurally implied to be the 4-player hit-fed source form from Plans 10/11/14 but not source-confirmed. Drills 3–6 are captured in full.

**Drill 1 — Best Warm Up Ever** *(name only; standard repeated source family)*: Source text identical to the universal BAB opener captured in Plans 1–16. Plan 17 extends the universal-opener evidence to the Game Play cluster — `Best Warm Up Ever` is now confirmed as the BAB default opener across **all four captured single-focus clusters** (passing, setting, attacking, defense) **and** the first captured Game Play plan.

**Drill 2 — Triangle Setting** *(name only; structurally implied 4-player hit-fed variant)*: No source text provided in the Plan 17 founder capture. Same status as Plans 15 and 16 Drill 2 — structurally implied to be the same 4-player hit-fed source form captured in Plans 10/11/14, but not source-confirmed. Plan 17 extends the Triangle Setting (4p hit-fed) name-only chain to **three plans (15, 16, 17)** alongside three source-detail captures (Plans 10, 11, 14), bringing the total Triangle Setting (4p hit-fed) plan reference count to **six plans**.

**Drill 3 — Race to 5 HL and CS** (20 min): Player 1 serves to Players 2 and 3, who are **both left sides** (i.e., two attackers compete on the same drill). Player 4 sets for them. Players 2 and 3 race to get 5 shots in a marked accuracy box; once one player hits 5, the players switch jobs. Round 1 is high line; Round 2 is cut shots.

This is a **new competitive race format** distinct from prior captured pressure formats:

- `+3/-3 Highlines - Cut Shots / HL` (Plan 7 Drill 4): point-spread-to-3 scoring on a single accuracy box, one attacker.
- `2 Ball Side Out` (Plan 7 Drill 6): two-shot-per-player alternating accuracy with bounded reps (5+5).
- **Plan 17 Drill 3 `Race to 5 HL and CS`**: first-to-5 race format with **two attackers competing simultaneously** on the same drill, alternating attempts via the server's feed. New competitive structure: race-to-N rather than spread or bounded reps.

The drill is **per-shot** (Round 1 HL, Round 2 CS) and reuses Plan 7's accuracy-box convention, confirming the per-shot-variant pattern (T8) and the accuracy-box convention from Plan 7. Importantly, the two-attacker structure is new — prior accuracy drills assumed one attacker at a time. The race-to-N format is also a sibling but distinct competitive structure to existing wrappers (Mini Games to 7, 14-15 Games to 21, etc.).

**Drill 4 — 10 Sideouts** (20 min): Each player gets a chance to receive 10 serves in a row to side out **against a full defense**. Keep track of each player's final score to make it competitive.

This is a **new measurement format** — the first BAB drill that explicitly measures **sideout rate over a fixed trial count** (10 serves) for competitive comparison. Distinct from prior pressure formats:

- `3 Before 5` family: race-to-N pressure between teams (serving team to 3 vs receiving team to 5).
- `+3/-3` family: point-spread accuracy scoring.
- **Plan 17 Drill 4 `10 Sideouts`**: per-player **sideout-rate-out-of-10** measurement — the score is the count of successful sideouts in a fixed-trial block, and the trial block is per-player.

The "full defense" cue implies blocker + defender on the serving side, making this a 4+ player drill. The structure is FIVB-compatible: it matches FIVB Level I Coaches Manual Ch VII's "Successful reps in a row" and "Athlete termination" measurement modes (the player's block ends after 10 serves regardless of outcome), confirming the cross-source measurement-mode finding from `docs/research/practice-plan-authoring-synthesis.md`.

**Drill 5 — 3 Before 5** (30 min): Team A receives all serves. Their goal is to side out 5 times before they get stopped 3 times. **If they score 5, they secure their point by serving and winning that point — and if they win it, they get a BIG point.** Play until 1 team gets 3-4 BIG points. **Switch sides of the court after 2 BIG points.**

This is the **same source form as the existing 3 Before 5 family** (Plans 1, 4, 8) with a **new BIG point elevation mechanic**. The base drill is unchanged: receive serves, race-to-5-sideouts versus 3-stops. The new mechanic adds an outcome-elevation overlay: **achieving the win condition (5 sideouts) does not directly score; instead, it earns the right to a serve-and-win sub-game that elevates the win to a "BIG point."** This is structurally distinct from prior captured 3 Before 5 variants:

- Plan 1 Drill 8 `3 Before 5 (Serve 1 Player)`: base form, score directly on win condition.
- Plan 8 Drill 7 `3 Before 5 (Serve 1 Player) (SHOTS ONLY)`: rule-restricted variant (no hard-driven attacks).
- **Plan 17 Drill 5 `3 Before 5` with BIG points**: outcome-elevation variant where the win condition becomes a sub-game gate rather than the score.

The BIG point mechanic is a **new kind of scoring overlay** — distinct from rule-restriction (Plan 8, narrows behavior) and rule-augmentation (Plan 11 with-blocker -1 penalty, adds penalty). It's an **outcome-elevation rule**: the win condition triggers a sub-game whose result is what scores. This adds a fourth scoring overlay kind to the captured set:

1. Rule-restriction (Plan 8 `SHOTS ONLY`, `(only shots)`, `Round N ONLY`)
2. Rule-augmentation (Plan 11 `with Blocker` -1 penalty, Plan 15 `win by 2`)
3. Tiebreaker (Plan 16 `third-to-15`)
4. **Outcome elevation (Plan 17 `BIG point` sub-game gate)** — new

The "switch sides after 2 BIG points" rule is an additional micro-rule for environmental fairness (sun, wind), structurally similar to Plan 9 Drill 8's `Set to 21` "switch at 7s" rule. This is **side-switch as a composable scoring rule fragment** — independent of base score-to-N, tiebreaker-to-M, and win-by-margin extension.

**Drill 6 — Games to 21** (remainder of practice): Play a normal match to 21 points. **If you have time, complete the final set to 15 regardless of who wins or losses.**

This is the **traditional beach volleyball match format** captured for the first time as a Plan 17 wrapper. Distinct from prior captured wrappers:

- `14-15 Games to 21` (Plans 9, 10, 11, 13, 14, 15): compressed-start variant where the score begins at 14-15 instead of 0.
- `Set to 21` (Plan 9 Drill 8): full single set with side switches at 7s.
- `Best of 3, Match to 21` (Plan 16 Drill 7): best-of-3 series with `third-to-15` tiebreaker.
- **Plan 17 Drill 6 `Games to 21`**: the simplest game-time wrapper — play a normal match to 21, and if there's time left, play a final set to 15 regardless of match outcome.

The "final set to 15 regardless of outcome" rule is structurally interesting: it **detaches the third-set-to-15 tiebreaker from the match-deciding role** and makes it a time-fill mechanism. This is the first BAB capture where a third-set-to-15 is played for **practice continuation** rather than to break a tie. It supports a new modeling consideration: scoring rules can be **conditioned on time-remaining** rather than only on match state. Future Volleycraft session-builder logic could distinguish "scheduled" vs "if-time-allows" wrapper extensions.

### Practice Plan 17 — synthesis and catalog markup (2026-05-04)

Plan 17 is the **first BAB Game Play cluster plan captured at source-detail level**, and the first cluster representative for what the adversarial review on `docs/research/practice-plan-authoring-synthesis.md` named as the cluster best positioned to test whether the captured BAB plan grammar is genuinely focus-agnostic. Plan 17 also matters because the founder's "defensive" labeling discrepancy is itself a source signal: Plan 17 is **next in BAB's drill-book ordering** after the Defense cluster (Plans 12–16), and BAB's TOC labels Plans 17–20 as Game Play. Future captures from Plans 18–20 should resolve any remaining ambiguity about cluster-labeling conventions.

Five structural observations matter for future Volleycraft plan-builder work:

1. **The Plan 17 grammar fits the captured six-slot focus-agnostic spine** — partial confirmation of the "spine generalizes across all focus areas" claim (and also a partial test of the adversarial review's prediction that Game Play might falsify the claim). Plan 17's slot mapping:
  - **Slot 1 (Opener):** Best Warm Up Ever (Drill 1) — universal opener confirmed across all clusters.
  - **Slot 2 (Primer):** Triangle Setting (Drill 2) — the 4p hit-fed primer recurrent across clusters.
  - **Slot 3 (Per-shot technique / accuracy):** Race to 5 HL and CS (Drill 3) — per-shot accuracy work scaled to a competitive race; structurally novel format but conceptually fits the per-shot-technique slot.
  - **Slot 4 (Movement / position):** **skipped** — Game Play plans don't need a movement primer once warm-up is done; the players are already in transition mode.
  - **Slot 5 (Read / decision / pressure overlay):** 10 Sideouts (Drill 4) — per-player sideout-rate measurement under pressure.
  - **Slot 6 (Live-feed / live-point transfer):** 3 Before 5 with BIG points (Drill 5) — sideout race with point-elevation sub-game.
  - **Slot 7 (Competitive wrapper):** Games to 21 (Drill 6) — full match with `final set to 15`.
   The Plan 17 grammar **fits five of the six slots** (skipping slot 4) and instantiates each fitted slot with **game-play-specific content**, which is consistent with the adversarial review's prediction that Game Play plans would test the spine but **inconsistent** with the prediction that they would falsify it. The spine carries; only the slot 4 movement-primer is dropped, which is structurally honest because Game Play plans assume players are already moving.
2. **Plan 17 introduces a fourth scoring-overlay kind** — outcome elevation. The captured BAB scoring-overlay set (T9 in the synthesis doc) previously had three kinds: rule-restriction (Plan 8), rule-augmentation (Plan 11, Plan 15 `win by 2`), and tiebreaker (Plan 16 `third-to-15`). Plan 17's BIG point mechanic adds a fourth: an outcome-elevation rule where achieving the win condition triggers a sub-game whose result is what actually scores. This matters because it confirms BAB's scoring-overlay grammar is **richer than Thesis T9's two patterns** (restriction + augmentation) and instead has **at least four composable rule kinds**. T9 should be sharpened to acknowledge outcome-elevation as a third pattern; T9's "rule-restriction ↔ rule-augmentation" symmetry framing is incomplete.
3. **The `10 Sideouts` measurement format is the first BAB drill explicitly using FIVB's "Successful reps in a fixed trial count" measurement mode** (Level I Coaches Manual Ch VII p. 122 measurement modes). This is **strong cross-source convergence** — the FIVB measurement-mode taxonomy now has BAB instantiations across at least three modes (Successful reps, Athlete termination, Successful reps in a row in 14-15 Games to 21). Future Volleycraft `successMetric` taxonomy work should consider FIVB's six measurement modes as the source-canonical taxonomy, with BAB providing the drill-grammar instantiations.
4. **The Race to 5 format with two competing attackers introduces a new participant-structure pattern.** Prior captured 4-player drills had role-differentiated participant structures (server / passer / setter / target, or attacker / blocker / defender / setter). Plan 17 Drill 3 has **two role-symmetric attackers** competing simultaneously, alternating via the shared server's feed. This is structurally distinct from Plan 5 Drill 8 `Mini Games to 7 (Two Players Battle)` (also two-attacker but as a battle, not a race) and from Plan 8's per-shot HL/CS drills (one attacker, sibling per-shot variants). Future Volleycraft drill metadata may need a `participantStructure` axis distinguishing role-differentiated, role-symmetric-cooperative, and role-symmetric-competitive structures.
5. **The "switch sides after 2 BIG points" rule and "final set to 15 regardless of outcome" rule together argue that scoring rules are even more composable than Thesis T9 / Plan 15 / Plan 16 captured.** Plan 9's `Set to 21` had "switch at 7s"; Plan 15 added `win by 2`; Plan 16 added `third-to-15` tiebreaker; Plan 17 adds **side-switch-on-N-events** and **conditional-extension-if-time-allows**. The captured BAB scoring grammar now has **at least six independent composable rule kinds**:
  - Base score-to-N (varies: 7, 21, 5)
  - Tiebreaker-to-M (Plan 16 `third-to-15`)
  - Win-by-margin extension (Plan 15 `win by 2`)
  - Side-switch trigger (Plan 9 `at 7s`, Plan 17 `at 2 BIG points`)
  - Outcome-elevation gate (Plan 17 `BIG point` sub-game)
  - Conditional-extension-if-time-allows (Plan 17 `final set to 15 regardless`)
   Future Volleycraft scoring metadata should treat these as **six independent parameters** rather than enumerating each combination as a separate scoring type. This sharpens Plan-Builder Thesis T-Plan-10 (composable scoring rules) in `docs/research/practice-plan-authoring-synthesis.md` from "three or four independent rules" to "at least six independent rule kinds."

Key synthesis against the other source archives:

- **Same Tier 3+ stance for all Plan 17 novel work.** None of `attack`, `defense`, or "game play" is a shipped Volleycraft `SkillFocus`, and there are no current attack / defense / game-play drills in `app/src/data/drills.ts`. Plan 17's three new drills (Drills 3, 4, 6) plus the BIG point augmentation of Drill 5 sit entirely in the Tier 3+ backlog. The competitive wrapper drills (3, 4, 5, 6) are session-shape constructs that would belong in `app/src/data/archetypes.ts` (or a future game-play archetype family), not as drill records in `app/src/data/drills.ts`.
- **Plan 17 confirms the captured BAB grammar generalizes to game-play emphasis** — but this should be read as a **partial test pass, not a full validation.** Plans 18–20 remain uncaptured. The strongest claim Plan 17 supports is "the spine fits a Game Play plan with one slot (movement) intentionally skipped"; the strongest claim it supports against the adversarial review's prediction is "Plan 17 does not falsify the spine; it instantiates it."
- **Plan 17 falsifies one specific framing.** The synthesis doc's `Captured Plan Grammar Templates` table previously claimed the spine generalizes across "passing, setting, attacking, defense" — with Game Play unconfirmed. Plan 17 partially confirms the generalization to game-play but **also reveals that the grammar's per-slot content shifts toward game-time formats** (race-to-N, sideout-rate measurement, full match). Future Volleycraft session-builder logic for game-play sessions should expect game-play-specific content per slot (not the same drill records as passing or defense slots), even when the slot structure is identical.
- **Plan 17 connects to FIVB Modified Games framing.** The Drill 5 BIG point overlay and Drill 6 Games to 21 with conditional extension both fit the FIVB Modified Games chapter pattern (rule deltas applied to a normal point), reinforcing Pattern P3 / M3 in the synthesis doc's `Patterns That May Be Coaching Template, Not BAB-Specific` section. Plan 17's scoring grammar is **more elaborate than FIVB's modified games chapter documents** — BAB has invested in scoring-overlay grammar specifically; FIVB's modified-games chapter is an inventory of 15 specific games rather than a composable rule set.
- **Plan 17 confirms the `3 Before 5` family is a reused source form across all four captured clusters.** `3 Before 5` now appears in Plan 1 (passing), Plan 4 (passing), Plan 8 (attacking with `SHOTS ONLY` rule restriction), and Plan 17 (game play with `BIG point` outcome elevation). The four-plan repetition rank places `3 Before 5` among the highest-priority catalog-add candidates per Thesis T13 (repetition signals priority); the BIG point variant is a **new schema requirement** (outcome-elevation rule kind) per the same thesis (novelty signals architecture).
